New Measures by the French Cabinet; Labor Bill Submitted to the Chamber of Deputies

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies convened at 4:00 PM, and Prime Minister Léon Blum presented several draft laws concerning labor and social issues, requesting:

* Implementation of a 40-hour work week;

* Two weeks of annual vacation with pay for workers;

* Unions to represent workers and sign labor contracts with employers;

* Elimination of the current salary reduction for low-level civil servants whose salaries are extremely meager;

* Elimination of the reduction in benefits for veterans.

Léon Blum also made a brief speech, stating that the labor unrest that had lasted for more than ten days had now been satisfactorily resolved, which was a cause for great joy. The Chamber of Deputies immediately decided to form a special committee of 33 members, including some opposition members, to review the wording of each of these draft laws and submit them for a vote at the end of this week. The Chamber of Deputies then adjourned and is scheduled to reconvene on Thursday. (Havas, 9th)

People's Livelihood Should Be Considered; Demanding Explanation from the Government on Two Points

(Paris) The Left Republican group in the Senate held a meeting today. Senator and Chairman Li Yi'an expressed surprise at some of the draft laws proposed by the cabinet (referring to the laws on social and labor issues proposed by Prime Minister Blum), believing that they would increase the cost of goods and the level of people's lives. If so, then the increase in wages for salaried workers would be futile. It was resolved that before the parliamentary vote on these draft laws, the cabinet should first be asked to explain two points:

* If prices rise in the future and exports are halted, what measures does the cabinet intend to take to remedy the situation?

* If French goods do not sell well in the future, leading to factory closures and an increase in unemployment, what measures does the cabinet intend to take to prevent this?

In addition, the group believes that attention should be paid to the fact that the two countries were originally closely related, but due to sanctions, there is some discord. Therefore, they hope that the issue of sanctions against Italy can be resolved quickly. (Havas, 9th)

Labor-Management Agreement Reached; Labor Unrest in Various Industries Gradually Resolved

(Paris) Labor unrest in various industries has been gradually resolved. Twelve thousand striking food delivery workers in the capital reached an agreement with store owners last night and are expected to return to work today. Employees of insurance companies and employers have also reached a compromise on the terms of resumption of work. Factories in the iron and steel, leather, woodworking, oil refining, and plating industries in the northern districts have all resumed work. Factory owners in the woolen industry in Roubaix have also accepted the workers' demands, and 80,000 workers are scheduled to return to work on Thursday. Ten thousand workers in the underwear industry in Troyes are also expected to return to work today. (Havas, 10th)

(Paris) Although labor unrest in most areas has been resolved due to individual agreements between labor and management, strikes continue to occur in some cities. For example, coal miners in Anzin, transportation, construction, and lead-iron workers in Toulouse, employees of some small department stores in the port of Bordeaux, and 10,000 textile workers in Reims have stopped working. In addition, labor unrest in Maubeuge has spread to the Sambre River basin, where the total number of striking metalworkers has reached as many as 20,000. (Havas, 10th)

(Paris) Many factories in the capital area and in the provinces, especially in the northeast and central regions, have resumed work. The labor dispute between the Hachette newspaper distribution company in the capital has ended, and all newspapers are being sold as usual. Labor and management in the construction industry are expected to reach a compromise tomorrow and resume work on Thursday morning. Labor and management in various industries in Lille in the north have also begun negotiations, but it is impossible to say at this time when the labor unrest will end. Some specific issues in the metallurgical industry have been resolved, and the only remaining issue is the increase in wages. It is difficult to reach a compromise in the textile industry. Negotiations in other major industries are based on a spirit of compromise, so the situation in each factory is very calm. (Havas, 9th)

(Paris) The new cabinet is now making every effort to prepare new legislative proposals to improve the living conditions of workers, but the wave of strikes continues to spread. The latest to join the strikes are waiters and workers in pastry shops. Waiters are demanding two hot meals a day, no fines for breaking objects, and not having to polish brassware. Porters are demanding that residents of the building should each have a key to the door to avoid knocking on the door late at night and disturbing the porter's sleep. At the same time, negotiations in the textile and metal industries are still ongoing. These people are not satisfied with the increase in wages of 7% to 15%, and many are demanding an increase of 40%. In the industries where strikers have now returned to work, wages have generally increased by 20% to 35%, causing prices to rise everywhere. (Reuters, 10th)

Pan-American Convention; More Than 20 Countries Participating

Non-Recognition of Land Seized by Force

(Uruguay Capital) On October 10, 1933, the American countries signed the Pan-American Treaty of Non-Aggression and Conciliation in the capital of Uruguay, based on the proposal of Argentine Foreign Minister Saavedra Lamas. Article 2 states that any land seized by force will not be recognized. The first fifteen countries signed the treaty, and more than twenty countries have joined since then. The Uruguayan Chamber of Deputies has also recently approved the treaty by a majority vote. (Havas, 9th)

Japan's New Agreement with the Puppet State; Abolition of Part of Extraterritorial Rights

(Changchun) The basic agreement on the abolition of part of Japan's extraterritorial rights in "Manchukuo" was signed at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Changchun at 3:00 PM on the 10th by Japanese Plenipotentiary Ambassador Kamekichi Ueda and "Manchukuo" Foreign Minister Yanqing Zhang. At the same time, the governments of Japan and Manchukuo issued the text of the agreement. The main text of the treaty is as follows:

The Government of the Great Japanese Empire, in accordance with the spirit of the Protocol between Japan and Manchukuo signed on September 15, 1932, in order to promote the sound development of "Manchukuo" and to further consolidate the close and inseparable relationship existing between Japan and Manchukuo (decided to gradually abolish) the extraterritorial rights now held by Japan in "Manchukuo" and to adjust or transfer the administrative rights of the South Manchurian Railway Zone. Therefore, the Government of Manchukuo, grateful for this decision of the Japanese Government, recognizes the necessity of ensuring and promoting the integrated development within the "Manchukuo" territory, which is closely related to Japan and Manchukuo. Therefore, both governments have agreed on the following regarding Japan's extraterritorial rights in "Manchukuo" and the administrative rights of the South Manchurian Railway Zone, focusing first on the residence and enjoyment of various rights and interests by Japanese nationals, as well as the applicable laws for taxation, industry, etc., in "Manchukuo":

Article 1: Japanese nationals shall be free to reside and travel within the territory of "Manchukuo" and may engage in commerce, industry, and other public and private businesses and occupations. They may also enjoy all rights relating to land. Japanese nationals shall not be treated less favorably than "Manchukuo" nationals in the enjoyment of all rights and interests within the territory of "Manchukuo."

Article 2: Japanese nationals within the territory of "Manchukuo" shall, in accordance with the provisions of the supplementary agreement to this treaty, comply with the administrative laws and regulations of "Manchukuo" regarding taxation, industry, etc. In the South Manchurian Railway Zone, the Japanese government recognizes that the aforementioned "Manchukuo" laws and regulations may be applied territorially in accordance with the provisions of the supplementary agreement to this treaty. Regarding the application of this article, Japanese nationals shall not be treated less favorably than "Manchukuo" nationals under any circumstances.

Article 3: The provisions of the preceding two articles shall also apply to corporations. Japanese corporations shall also be subject to these provisions.

Article 4: The provisions of this treaty shall not affect the rights, privileges, special features, and exemptions of specific Japanese nationals or corporations under special agreements between Japan and Manchukuo.

Article 5: This treaty shall be implemented from July 1, 1936, i.e., Kangde 3 (1936), July 1.

Article 6: The authentic texts of this treaty shall be in Japanese and Chinese. In case of any difference in interpretation between the Japanese text and the Chinese text, the Japanese text shall prevail. The following names, duly authorized by their respective governments, have signed this treaty as evidence.

Done in duplicate at Changchun on the tenth day of June in the eleventh year of Showa (1936), i.e., the tenth day of June in the third year of Kangde. Japanese Ambassador to "Manchukuo", Special Envoy Plenipotentiary Kamekichi Ueda, "Manchukuo" Minister of Foreign Affairs Yanqing Zhang. (Dōmei News Agency, 10th)

Additional Clauses

Changchun The plenipotentiary commissioners of Japan and "Manchukuo" have agreed on clauses regarding taxation matters between Japan and "Manchukuo" on the 10th. The main points are recorded as follows:

Article 1 The "Manchukuo" government will promptly take the necessary measures regarding the contents of the commercial lease rights held by Japanese nationals from the past, changing land ownership and other land rights.

Article 2 The scope of the administrative laws and regulations concerning taxation, industry, etc., that Japanese nationals should comply with under the provisions of Article 1 of the treaty, and the status of their application, shall first be decided by consultation between the Japanese Ambassador to Manchukuo and the Minister of Foreign Affairs of "Manchukuo."

Article 3 Japanese consulates may apply the relevant laws and regulations of "Manchukuo" in compliance with the general rules of consular jurisdiction. When imposing fines or declaring confiscation under this Article, the fines or confiscated goods shall be managed by the "Manchukuo" government.

Article 4 The Japanese government, based on separate agreements with the "Manchukuo" government, will abolish or transfer the administrative police force in Manchukuo by December 31, Showa 12 (1937) at the latest. Prior to the abolition or transfer, Article 2 of the treaty cannot be applied to the aforementioned railway zone in "Manchukuo" laws and regulations concerning courses and those specifically related to the administrative police power of the South Manchurian Railway Zone. The scope of laws and regulations related to the administrative police power of the South Manchurian Railway Zone shall be decided in advance through consultation between the Japanese Ambassador to Manchukuo and the Minister of Foreign Affairs of "Manchukuo."

Prior to the transfer of the administrative police force of the South Manchurian Railway Zone, in order to ensure a balance of the tax burden on Japanese nationals inside and outside the railway zone, from the date of implementation of the treaty, the "Manchukuo" national tax levied on Japanese nationals must be vigorously implemented equally in the railway zone. The "Manchukuo" government shall comply with separate agreements between Japan and Manchukuo and shall not levy local taxes on the aforementioned railway zone for civil engineering, education, sanitation, and other facilities of the Manchurian Railway Company in the Manchurian Railway Zone, unless they are handled by the company.

Articles 5 to 7 omitted.

Article 8 This agreement shall be implemented simultaneously with the treaty. This agreement shall be signed and initialed by the plenipotentiary commissioners of both countries as evidence. (Dōmei News Agency, 10th)

More than 1,000 representatives have a serious attitude. Landon is the most promising candidate for president.

The meeting adjourned at 12:33 and reopened at 8:00 in the evening. At that time, the temporary chairman will deliver a speech on the purpose of the meeting. Today's first meeting lacked enthusiasm. Party members were all serious. The meeting place was the lecture hall in this city. There were many well-known figures on the podium, such as Senator Vandenberg, former Senator Bemo Moses, former Secretary of the Treasury Mills, former Senator Leiter, conservative leader and former Senator Bingham, Congressman Martin, and former Governor Allen of Kansas. However, liberal leader Senator Borah was absent. Because Borah saw that Governor Landon of Kansas had a great hope of being elected as the next presidential candidate, he summoned representatives from Wisconsin in the hotel to discuss coping strategies. The meeting place was full of leaders from Landon's side. His propaganda officer Hamilton claimed that Landon could be elected in the first vote. However, other supporters said that they were prepared to make slight concessions to Borah's proposal. Now, Borah's request seems to make the Landon faction the most uneasy. On the one hand, various permissions have been granted to representatives of the eastern states, while Borah insists on implementing a purge and rejuvenation movement within 48 hours. He is very dissatisfied with Landon's tendency to compromise. Representatives from states such as New York and California seemed to be trying to pressure Landon today to overturn Borah's request. Landon: 468 votes

Borah: 115 votes

Knox (Chicago publisher): 90 votes

Taft (son of former president): 47 votes

Vandenberg (Senator): 45 votes

Meekin (Judge): 23 votes

Dickinson (Senator): 22 votes

Nice (Governor of Maryland): 16 votes

Undecided: 177 votes

The conference has a total of 1,003 representatives. To be nominated as a candidate, one must have 502 votes. It is difficult to predict the vice presidential candidate today. The most promising candidate is the temporary chairman Steiwell. Judging from today's situation, Landon has a good chance of succeeding in the first vote. However, if three or four votes cannot obtain a majority, it may become a stalemate. Landon's side is very worried that Borah will see that the party's platform on issues such as currency, diplomacy, and industrial patents cannot fully satisfy him, and he will fight for principles. Borah is good at giving speeches and can move the audience. Landon will be greatly hindered. Once Landon is defeated, Vandenberg is quite hopeful. (9th National Telegram)

Cleveland - The Republican National Convention opened here at 10 o'clock last night. Senator Steiwell from Oregon delivered an opening speech. The speech was very long, and its general meaning advocated that the United States should adopt an isolationist policy and strictly abide by it in politics, economy, spirit, and society. He also fiercely attacked President Roosevelt, saying that based on patriotism, the President and his political allies should be forced to step down, especially Roosevelt, who must be regarded as a "foreign person in disguise" rather than an American. He also said that once the Republican Party is in power, it must abolish the current "New Deal" and replace it with "American Politics" in order to communicate the opinions of the Democratic and Republican parties without any barriers. The so-called "New Deal" has many malpractices. If we want to remedy it and revitalize it, the various principles contained in "American Politics" must be implemented. The main points of these principles are: free competition in all industries and not be restrained, just like marching an army; artificial bureaucratic politics must be eliminated; an isolationist policy must be adopted internationally; and new protectionism must be implemented in tariffs. "Thanks to its geographical location, the United States does not need to rely on other countries, which is a blessing from heaven. The government must use this special situation and avoid involvement in the affairs of other countries. This is the government's duty to the people," he said. After the speech, the representatives followed the usual practice of parading in the meeting place in teams, with music and cheers for the important party figures one by one. The meeting adjourned at midnight. The conference is now scheduled to continue this afternoon, and it is generally expected that important decisions can be made by evening. (10th Havas Telegram)

Japanese Side Maintains Silence on Diplomacy; Japanese Consulate General in Tianjin Strengthens Organization; Kuwashima Arrives in Tianjin to Convey Diplomatic Policy

Tianjin Gradually Returns to Calm; Authorities Strive to Maintain Order

Tianjin Dispatch: A week ago, the bombing of the Beining Railway caused unrest in Tianjin and Beijing, and rumors spread like wildfire. At the same time, personnel changes in a section of Hebei and Chahar were also rumored, causing widespread anxiety. By the end of last week, the rumors had gradually subsided and people's minds had calmed down as the authorities maintained calm and there were no diplomatic incidents. Although the Japanese side has not formally stated that it does not attach importance to the railway bombing incident, according to a spokesperson from the Japanese military headquarters, investigating the background is extremely difficult. Before a full understanding is reached, no statement will be made, so this matter will be delayed for a long time and will likely fade away. The Japanese military headquarters has adopted Huaibei diplomatic policies ever since Tashiro assumed his post in the middle of last month. However, on Wednesday, the third day of last week, Tashiro acted on his own initiative and convened a meeting of staff officers of the Japanese garrison, at which three important decisions were made: (1) To encourage the officers and take responsibility for advancing and completing the important mission of the garrison, based on the military's ironclad principles for North China. (2) To implement the new line of co-existence and co-prosperity in accordance with the firm instructions of the Empire. (3) To closely liaise with and support the new Consul General, Tajiri Aiyi, of the Tianjin Consulate General in accordance with the military's intentions and to give full play to his aggressive diplomatic skills. Tajiri was appointed to Tianjin with the rank of First Secretary of the Japanese Embassy in China and as concurrently acting Consul General of Tianjin, and was also designated as the top-ranking official in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The purpose of this assignment is to integrate the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' policies with the Tianjin Garrison Headquarters and to realize what is called "diplomatic unity." The Tianjin Consulate General has strengthened its organization since June 10th to facilitate liaison with the Japanese military headquarters. Kuwashima, the Director-General of the East Asia Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, acting on the orders of the Japanese Foreign Minister Arita, will arrive in Tianjin on the 11th after meeting with the leaders of the Japanese Kwantung Army in the Northeast to give instructions and convey the unified diplomatic policy. Currently, if the Hebei-Chahar authorities do not request negotiations on the Hebei and Chahar matters, the Japanese side will temporarily maintain a cool attitude and will not begin its direct policy until the military and consulate are in seamless contact. Currently, there are still many rumors in Tianjin,传闻相传前任苏皖巡使某、前任第五路军总指挥某, it is rumored that a certain former Superintendent of Jiangsu and Anhui and a certain former Commander-in-Chief of the Fifth Route Army are doing their best to recruit die-hard followers and form them into plainclothes teams, which have already obtained several thousand people, who are all lurking in the suburbs of Tianjin and in a certain concession, and will take actions unfavorable to the overall situation in Hebei and Chahar. Bai Jianwu, who caused trouble in Fengtai on the outskirts of Beijing last year, is also active in this group. Although the matter has not yet been launched, there are also many people who hope for extravagant things. A certain Chairman, a certain Mayor, a certain Chief of Public Security, and a certain Salt Commissioner of Changlu, all regard themselves as central figures in the future situation. Fearing that the Tianjin's security will become chaotic, the Hebei-Chahar Political Council has ordered the Security Commander Liu Jialuan to properly plan prevention methods and has ordered Liu to concurrently serve as the Director of the Hebei Province Wuhe Water Police Bureau and the Maritime Police Bureau, unifying the command of the water and land military police, and strictly deploying forces inside and outside the city, which is equivalent to a temporary garrison commander. On Thursday, Liu, acting Security Commander, convened Sun Weidong, Director of the Tianjin Public Security Bureau, as well as company commanders and above of the Security Force, platoon leaders and above of the garrison troops, and military and police officers to discuss thorough defense measures. From that day on, they have focused their efforts on monitoring the activities of a certain inspecting envoy and a certain commander-in-chief in a certain concession. Liu Jialuan told the press that although there are many rumors in the city, they will not affect security. He has agreed with Sun Weidong, Director of the Law Enforcement Bureau, to do everything possible to maintain security and not allow a few people to harbor evil intentions and plot disturbances. If it is absolutely necessary, they will not hesitate to make major sacrifices. As for diplomacy, that is a separate matter and is not within his responsibility, and the highest authorities will be responsible for it. (8th)

After Li Shengda Was Assassinated, His Wife and Son Both Died for Him; On the Seventh Night After Li's Death, His Wife and Son Died One After Another After Lighting Paper Offerings

Taiyuan Dispatch: Li Shengda, a member of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang and Commander of the 19th Army, was assassinated on the 31st of last month in Lishi. After hearing the news at her residence in the provincial capital, his wife immediately took a car to visit him. When she arrived in Fenyang, she learned the definite news of Li's death and immediately fainted. It took a great deal of effort from the accompanying staff to revive her, and she immediately returned to the provincial capital by the same car. Li's wife was overwhelmed with grief and determined to die. In her sorrow, she repeatedly told people that once the Commander's coffin returned to Bing and arrangements were made for his funeral, she would make her intentions clear. For several days, she had been weeping all day long and had stopped eating and drinking. Although relatives and friends had tried to persuade her in every way, they were unable to change her mind. The family had no choice but to take extra care to prevent accidents. Until the afternoon of the 5th of this month, she had only consumed half a bowl of rice soup.

Light Rain Descends; The Course of Events

The 5th was the seventh day after Li's death, and relatives and friends came to mourn in an endless stream. Around 10:00 PM, a light rain suddenly began to fall. The people in charge of the household, fearing that a heavy rain would come soon, gathered the wreaths and flower arrangements in the courtyard and moved them to the corridor outside the mourning hall. Li's coffin, after being transported back from Lishi, was placed in the north hall of the west courtyard of the residence. The east and west rooms of the hall were Li's inner chambers during his lifetime. There was another eaves corridor outside the hall. Around 12:00 AM that night, just as the monks and Taoists were chanting scriptures and burning paper offerings, there was a slight breeze, which caused sparks to fly high. Due to carelessness, the flower arrangements that had been moved to the front of the corridor were ignited. The people in charge immediately tried their best to put out the fire.

Sitting Still, Unwavering in Her Determination to Die

At that time, Li's wife and her biological eldest son, Wenlong, were mourning in the west room of the north hall. Seeing the fire raging in the room, they immediately led the son to the mourning hall to call for help. Their attitude was calm and they showed no panic. The son, only seven years old, was at his mother's side. The wife shouted to quickly take my son out, and those around her braved the fire to enter and first carried the son out. They then re-entered to rescue the wife. At this time, the wife closed her eyes and shouted loudly, "My son has been taken out, don't worry about me!" This delayed the rescue. Those around her were extremely alarmed and pulled her out, but the wife was determined not to move. She struggled and plunged into the fire, holding the threshold firmly with her hands. For a time, she could not be pulled out. By the time everyone struggled to free her, the wife was already on her last breath. Because the time was too long, the son was also severely burned. That night, they were sent to the Chuanzhi Hospital by car. By 10:00 AM on the morning of the 6th, the wife was beyond saving and passed away.

Braving the Fire to Rescue the Coffin

The firefighters desperately rescued the wife and quickly braved the fire to rescue Li's coffin. Fortunately, the north hall had windows opening on the other side, and there was a small open space outside the windows. Everyone entered the hall and lifted the coffin out through the windows and placed it on the ground. At this time, the fire was raging, threatening to spread like wildfire. Fortunately, the rescue efforts were effective in extinguishing the fire outside the courtyard. As for the fire inside the house (i.e., inside the north hall mourning hall), only a part of the paper-covered ceiling was burned from the doorway to the back windows, and the rest was unaffected. There was no other damage. According to eyewitnesses, at that time, everyone was in a panic. After moving Li's coffin out, they first extinguished the fire in the courtyard. As for the fire inside the house, it was soon extinguished on its own. In the darkness, it seemed that there was a divine presence. It was indeed a great stroke of luck amidst misfortune. The fire outside the courtyard was not completely extinguished until around 1:00 or 2:00 AM.

The Wife is Dressed for Burial; The Son is in a Coma

After the fire broke out, Feng Pengzhu, the Adjutant of the Pacification Headquarters, Rong Honglu, the Commander of the Garrison, and Cheng Shurong, the Director of Public Security, rushed to direct the firefighting. At the same time, they also telephoned Yan Xishan to report the situation. Yan, upon hearing the news, immediately ordered doctors from the Chuanzhi Hospital to rush to treat the injured. After Li's wife and son were admitted to the hospital, emergency surgery was performed. However, the wife and son's whole bodies were severely burned, and their skin and flesh were completely ulcerated. Their body temperatures dropped to the lowest levels. Although every effort was made to save them, the results were minimal. Li's wife died at the hospital at 10:00 AM on the 6th, and the son died at the hospital at 4:00 PM. After Li's wife died, Yan was extremely saddened by her martyrdom. He immediately ordered that a coffin made of Phoebe zhennan wood be purchased and that the body be dressed for burial at the hospital. The coffin was transported to Li's residence on the afternoon of the 6th. Yan also sent Division Commander Wang Jingguo to inspect the Li residence and comfort the family.

Inspecting the Tragic Scene at the Li Residence

The reporter went to the Li residence on the morning of the 6th to inspect the scene. Li's coffin was still placed in the middle of the north hall. Inside the north hall, except for the ceiling, which was partially burned, the traces of the fire outside the courtyard were extremely widespread. The pillars in front of the north hall corridor, the east and west rooms, and the sky canopy in the courtyard were all burned to a charred black. However, all four houses were unharmed. From this, it can be seen that the rescue efforts were effective. It was reported that in addition to the efforts of the family's stable hands, the Public Security Bureau's fire brigade also rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm. Li's wife, Wang, was 30 years old and from Jincheng. She had been with Commander Li for more than ten years, and their relationship was extremely close. The wife had two sons. The eldest son, Wenlong, was only seven years old and studied at the Kindergarten of the National Teachers' Affiliated Elementary School. The other son was only two years old and was cared for by a nanny. When the reporter left the Li residence after the inspection, he saw the nanny leading him outside the door, playing innocently and oblivious to what had happened. Seeing this situation and the wife's martyrdom, one could not help but be moved to tears. (June 6th)

Rice Shortage in Northern Fujian; Once a Rice-Producing Area, It Now Needs Foreign Rice to Alleviate the Situation

Fuzhou Dispatch: Northern Fujian was originally a rice-producing area. In recent years, due to the disturbances caused by the Red Bandits, farmers have fled and fields have been abandoned, resulting in a situation where areas that used to transport rice to Fuzhou for sale now have to purchase foreign rice from Fuzhou to alleviate the situation. The decline of the rural economy is evident. Since the suppression of the Red disaster the year before last, farmers have gradually returned and engaged in farming, and the food supply has been somewhat self-sufficient. However, due to poor harvests last autumn, there was not much rice in storage, and a famine occurred in the summer of this year. In the past ten days or so, rice prices in Nanping, Jian'ou, Pucheng, Chong'an, Jiangle, and Shunchang counties have soared, increasing from nine yuan per stone to twelve yuan, and they continue to rise. The county governments and chambers of commerce have sent telegrams to the provincial government requesting relief. The provincial government has telegraphed Shanghai, requesting that a large batch of sea rice be transported to Fujian to be transshipped to northern Fujian. At the same time, more than 400 packages of rice stored in the provincial capital were transported to Yanping for relief. However, since the end of spring, the provincial capital has experienced two floods, and low-lying fields have been submerged, resulting in significant losses of seedlings. Farmers are currently sorting things out, and about three-tenths of the seedlings will rot. At this time of year, when the new crop is not yet available, the local rice production in various townships is already insufficient. Moreover, with the supply from northern Fujian cut off, the price of rice has also increased from ten yuan to eleven yuan per stone in the provincial capital. Fortunately, the counties of Ningde, Fu'an, and Xiapu in eastern Fujian had very good harvests last autumn and still have surplus rice this summer. Recently, rice merchants Rongfeng and Qinghe and other firms have successively requested the county chambers of commerce to forward requests to the Minhou County Government for the issuance of passports to facilitate the purchase and transportation of rice to the province for relief. To date, many days have passed, but no passports have been issued, and the rice merchants have not been able to set out. However, a batch of sea rice has arrived, which has provided some assistance. Therefore, the price of rice has remained around eleven yuan and has not continued to increase. (June 6th)

Guangdong Province Actively Trains Administrative Personnel

Plans to Establish an Administrative Personnel Training Institute; Graduates Will Be Assigned to Assist County Magistrates

Guangzhou Dispatch: The implementation of Guangdong's first three-year plan was completed at the end of the 24th year, and it has been quite successful. However, due to financial difficulties in various counties, it was not fully implemented. In order to continue to complete the plan, the authorities have drafted a second three-year administrative plan, selecting essential parts of the previous plan that were not implemented and incorporating considerations of the future environment in order to put politics on the right track and allow the people to rest and recuperate. The second plan has been drafted by various departments and submitted to the provincial government. After the directors of the departments return from inspecting the various counties, they will convene a meeting to make a decision so that the plan can be implemented as soon as possible on July 1st of this year. However, it is reported that the authorities believe that good government lies not in many words but in how it is implemented. However, even with a plan, if those who implement it do not work hard and simply go through the motions, it is all for naught. Since the county is an autonomous unit, the county magistrate's responsibilities are important, and it is appropriate to select talent, but it is also essential to have people to assist them. Therefore, the authorities, recognizing this, are currently planning to establish a provincial administrative personnel training institute (the name has not been fully decided). It will recruit students who have graduated from the advanced group of the first phase of the military academy's political advanced training program and students who have graduated from the special group and have not been assigned. They will be given further training to instill them with various types of administrative knowledge. The number of students is planned to be 100. After graduation, each county government will assign one student to assist the county magistrate in handling administrative affairs and implementing the second three-year administrative plan, thereby increasing the efficiency of administration. This matter is currently being planned. Once it is submitted to and passed by the Provincial Affairs Conference and approved by the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, it can be implemented as scheduled.

Songjiang Set a Deadline for River Dredging

The dredging of rivers in various districts of the county by requisitioning labor was previously ordered by the Construction Department to be carried out in accordance with the established business methods. Now, the department has ordered that all river courses that have not been dredged by the end of the year must be completed by the end of this month. The county government has ordered each district to complete all river courses that have not been completed by the 15th of the month and to report them immediately to be forwarded to the department for statistics.

Suzhou The Rent Riot Has Not Yet Ended

Residents of Xialian Township, Loumenwai, Xietang Town, rioted over rent and destroyed seven houses of the baojia heads in Yu Lane. Afterwards, they accused the security team of drowning a child. Hundreds of people flocked to Xietang Town and clashed with the security team. The child's body was inspected in the countryside on the morning of the 10th by Zhang Minsheng, a prosecutor from the local court, who confirmed that the child had drowned in the river. According to the statement from Zhu Zhu, a relative of the deceased, the deceased was her granddaughter, Zhu Ada, six years old. On the afternoon of the 8th, the security team went to Yu Lane to arrest people. Zhu, along with Li Shenshi and two others, were taken away by the team. At that time, Ada was carried on Zhu's back and was pushed into the river by a security team member, etc. It is now reported that the villagers are generally dissatisfied with this. On the afternoon of the 9th, the city specially dispatched additional security teams to Xietang Town to increase defenses, and put up foot patrols in the evening. Xietang Elementary School was closed for one day that day, and the situation remains serious.

Wuxi Merchants and Residents Seize Smuggled Goods

Tong Maoyu Cargo Firm, located at the entrance of Jiangyin Lane, Beithang, is opened by Zhou Binrong and is quite prosperous. Yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM, more than 40 members of the anti-smuggling team organized by merchants and residents of Beithang, together with police officer Zhong Zhixiang of the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau and Wu Rongmo of the First Detachment of the 4th Regiment, went to the firm to search for smuggled goods. As a result, they found ten boxes of salmon (commonly known as tung oil fish), which were immediately sent to the county party headquarters for disposition. Sun Xiangfeng, the party committee member, received them and ordered the merchants and residents to return to their homes. He also telegraphed the county magistrate to discuss the disposal methods. However, according to the firm, the salmon was not smuggled goods. They specifically sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce requesting the Party Headquarters to return the goods. The Chamber of Commerce also believes that this matter is significant and is waiting for the authorities to handle it.

Changshu County Government Bans Temple Fairs

The Old City God Temple here has not held a temple fair for more than ten years. Some well-intentioned people have initiated a temple fair to be held on the 13th and 14th of this month, citing the need to revive the sluggish market. The whole county is ecstatic because the City God Fair, which has not been seen for more than ten years, is being restored. The ceremonial guard is particularly grand. Therefore, hotels and restaurants have already been fully booked, and the hotel industry has increased room rates by 20% as a donation for planes for Chiang's birthday. In addition, various merchants have also stocked up on goods to meet the demand of the fair market. The Xihu Automobile Company has also decided to open special buses from various ports starting on the 12th of this month to attract foreign visitors. Unexpectedly, the party headquarters believes that the temple fair is superstitious and has sent a letter to the county to ban it. At the moment the county government has posted a notice. However, since the fair is approaching and all preparations have been completed, it is difficult to forcibly stop it. It is reported that the Public Security Bureau will increase its forces to prevent disturbances at that time. However, merchants and residents believe that the fair market is sufficient to prosper the market and will jointly petition.

Changzhou Notice Not to Discuss Stolen Coal

The Wuyi County Chamber of Commerce recently saw reports that stolen coal from Liujiang landed in Chengyi, causing a reaction from people in that area, and there was news that it would be transported to Changzhou for sale by barge. As it has been found that this stolen coal was previously ordered to be informed to Yongda Fumei Coal Company that it should not be undertaken to sell it, the coal number was informed to comply with this order on time. Recently, as this coal is being transported to Changzhou for sale, it should be complied with in accordance with the previous order not to undertake the sale of it. On the 9th, the Yongda Fumei Coal Company and the Coal and Iron Industry Association were specially notified to comply with this order, and a notice was published in the newspaper to the entire coal industry to uphold justice and never undertake the sale of this coal.

Jiangyin Loyalty Shrine Changed to Martyrs' Shrine

The county government has ordered the construction of a Martyrs' Shrine. County Magistrate Yuan has decided after a meeting to rebuild the original Loyalty Shrine on Zhong Street. A construction committee has been organized, and Wu Shuying has been appointed as the director of general affairs. However, the Loyalty Shrine is full of memorial tablets of officials, soldiers, and people who died in the previous Qing Hongyang Rebellion, and the words "Royal Qing" make replacement difficult. It has been decided to set aside the center to set up a martyrs' memorial tablet to save costs.

Danyang Poor Harvest of Wheat

Recently, with continuous overcast and rainy weather, the wheat harvest has declined. Therefore, at the moment when they are on the market, there are not many goods to be seen in the market. Barley is priced at four yuan per dan, and wheat is priced at six yuan per dan. If the goods do not surge into the market, the price will continue to rise.

Nantong The Reclamation Area Investigation Team Arrives in Tong

The Shanghai Banking Group, the Cotton Industry Control Association, and the China Yarn Factory Association have jointly formed the Northern Jiangsu Reclamation Area Investigation Team. The group of 30 people arrived in Tong at 9:00 AM on the 11th and transferred to Dongtai, Yancheng, and Funing, ending at Baojiadun. The round trip is scheduled for ten days, and they will return to Shanghai from Nantong on the 20th. Zhu Yinglan, the Chief of the Disaster Relief Committee, and Ge Tan, the Commissioner of the Southern District, are also traveling with them.

Gaoyou New Wheat Enters the Market

Outside the South Gate of this county is an area where old grain businesses converge. The new wheat has now entered the market. On the 8th, the price was five yuan and eight jiao per stone, which is more than two yuan cheaper than old goods.

Ningbo Piracy Rampant in Ninghai

The residents along the coast of Ninghai have always relied on fishing for a living. There are more than 150 fishing boats. On the 3rd of this month, near Nanjiushan, they suddenly encountered more than 50 pirates, each holding sharp weapons, who took away more than 50 fishermen and three fishing boats. There has been no news of them to date. The fishermen's families have made every effort to inquire, but there is still no information about their whereabouts. They are all in a state of panic. It is rumored that the bandits Jin Yutang and Huang Daoshou are responsible. The fishermen have already requested the county government to severely crack down on them.

Hangzhou A Wonderful Tale of Rekindling Wedding Vows

Mr. Cheng Zizhi, a famous scholar, traveled to Jiangsu in his early years as a Juren and served as an official with integrity. He has been highly regarded by the people of his hometown for handling charitable and public welfare affairs in his hometown after retiring from office in 1911. This year is the 80th birthday of Mr. Cheng and his wife, and the occasion of rekindling their wedding vows. However, Mr. Cheng, considering the instability of the current situation, strictly instructed his son Yangpo (currently a standing committee member of the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce) not to take any action. His humility and virtue are commendable. It is now reported that several of his best friends, such as Zhang Xuan Chu and Wang Fuchuan, have initiated a small banquet at home on the 17th of this month to celebrate. It is also heard that one of the people who escorted the bride when Mr. Cheng got married is still alive and will also be invited to participate at that time. However, it is not true that Mr. Cheng's age is 82 and his wife's age is 83 as reported in the Hangzhou newspaper some days ago, and the engagement of a certain important person from the provincial government to serve as the witness of their re-wedding vows.

Two Provinces Jointly Operate Fertilizer Plant

The Zhejiang Construction Department is working to improve the soil and implement the centralized import of chemical fertilizers, mixing and manufacturing nitrogen, phosphorus, and potassium fertilizers to facilitate farmers' use. The Jiangsu Construction Department has sent Agricultural Management Committee Deputy Director Zeng Jikuan to Zhejiang to discuss joint centralized management methods between Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. It has been decided in principle to jointly establish a mixed fertilizer manufacturing plant in Shanghai. The Zhenhai Phosphate Fertilizer Manufacturing Plant will also be jointly funded by Jiangsu Province, with an investment of 380,000 yuan from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank of China and the Jiangsu Farmers Bank, each investing half. The fertilizer required by the two provinces will be put out to tender in Shanghai on the 15th of this month, the bids will be opened on the 25th, the contract will be signed at the end of the month, and the centralized management will be implemented and the plant will be established starting on July 1st.

Immense Losses from Fire

At 6:20 PM on the 9th, a fire suddenly broke out at Huafeng Paper Mill's northern warehouse at No. 58 Xiahe Wooden Bridge in Gongbu, due to an electrical fault. The warehouse contained a large quantity of paper stock, causing the fire to spread rapidly. The fire was uncontrollable. Firefighters from the Public Security Bureau and other fire brigades rushed to the scene to extinguish the fire, which was finally put out after 1:00 AM on the 10th. Seven warehouses and a large amount of paper stock were destroyed, resulting in losses of over ten thousand yuan. The factory owner, Liu Guizhan, has been summoned by the Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Xiaoshan: Couple Commits Suicide Due to Silkworm Farming Losses

A Mr. and Mrs. Lu, residents of Shushan Village in the eastern part of Xiaoshan County, had been silkworm farmers. This silkworm season, the initial price of leaves was low, and they had fed their silkworms over two liang of leaves. Later, the price of leaves rose to over three yuan, requiring them to spend twenty to thirty yuan on leaves daily. They borrowed from all sides to purchase leaves and feed their silkworms, hoping for a high price for the cocoons. However, the price of cocoons dropped to two yuan and fifty cents, and few people were interested in buying them. They incurred losses of over two hundred yuan. Recently, they were pressured to repay their debts and were unable to do so. Mr. Lu attempted suicide on the night of the 7th of this month. His wife, seeing her husband's death and no prospect of repaying the debts, drowned herself in a small pond behind their house on the night of the 9th, after the funeral. Neighbors discovered her, but it was too late to save her. The couple ended their lives due to the financial losses from silkworm farming, which is truly tragic.

Boat Sinks in a Stormy Night Voyage

On the morning of the 9th, a night boat from Linshao, while traveling to Xie'en Bridge in Xixiaojiang, sank due to a leak in the hull caused by a heavy storm. Five passengers were on board and were rescued by fishing boats, narrowly avoiding drowning. However, various goods, including sacks of hemp, worth approximately four to five hundred yuan, sank to the bottom of the river, resulting in significant losses. As of noon on the 9th, the boat had not yet been salvaged. The boatman, Chen A'yuan, reported the incident to the Shaoxing boat dock for assistance, as well as the loss of the cargo.

Concentrating Strength is Appropriate to Overcome National Difficulties

Telegraphing the Central Government to Clearly Order a Stop to Action

Since reports emerged that the Guangdong and Guangxi armies had entered Hunan Province, public organizations in the city have been deeply shocked. Yesterday, they urged the Central Government to promptly stop this action and also advised the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities to unify their steps to save the nation, implement peaceful unity, and jointly resist aggression. A collection of telegrams is recorded below:

Upon hearing this, the whole country is in an uproar. At a time when national crisis is imminent, all with blood in their veins should be of one heart and one mind to overcome national difficulties. Therefore, unifying goals, concentrating strength, and aligning steps are all necessary limits. If preparations are not properly made and action is taken without authorization, how is this different from giving the enemy an opportunity, turning national salvation into national harm, and plunging our nation into an abyss from which it cannot recover? Your esteemed council holistically plans the overall situation and presides over the ultimate strategy. You should promptly order the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities to cease military action, gather the strength of the whole country, and prepare to quell the invaders. The haste of this telegram is paramount. Respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Special Municipality Second District Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party."

Telegraph Communications Around Hengzhou: Normal Transmission and Reception

According to the Central News Agency, it was reported in the evening newspapers of this city yesterday that telegraph communications in over thirty locations around Hengyang were once cut off yesterday (i.e., the day before yesterday) and that telegraph service had not been restored as of this morning (i.e., yesterday morning). The Central News Agency reporter stated last night, according to Shanghai Telegraph Bureau Director Bao Keyong, that this information is completely inaccurate. Telegraph communications around Hengyang have not been cut off recently. Transmission and reception between Changsha and Guangzhou are proceeding as usual.

City Education Authorities State: Order in All Schools is Normal

If Unruly Elements Are Discovered

They Will Of Course Be Firmly Dealt With

A Central News Agency reporter visited the city's education authorities yesterday to inquire about the situation in various schools. According to the response, since Premier Jiang's speech to the principals and student representatives of various universities last winter, all schools have been able to deeply understand the policies of the Central Government. Therefore, all schools have intensified the implementation of emergency education during this time of national crisis, and students are quite capable of conducting extracurricular research. After the spring break, students in all schools have returned to class as usual. Graduation classes are now conducting examinations. The joint graduation examination for middle school students has already been scheduled. Senior high schools are holding branch examinations, while junior high schools have switched to random examinations. Students in all schools are currently immersed in preparations. Although, recently, due to the current situation, some bored politicians have attempted to instigate student unrest, and a small number of students, under false pretenses, have secretly planned incitement and have encouraged others to avoid examinations, students in all schools have been able to understand the greater good, and teachers have provided appropriate guidance. Therefore, order in all schools is normal and has not been affected in the slightest, which is gratifying. However, it was recently discovered that some students in a certain grade of the attached middle school of the Sino-French Engineering College are suspected of being communists. The school authorities, fearing that this would affect other students, have advanced the start of the holiday. In the future, if unruly elements are discovered in any school, the authorities will surely deal with them firmly to avoid harming good students. At this time of national crisis and serious foreign aggression, we sincerely hope that young people will recognize the necessity of unity from top to bottom and, under the leadership of the Central Government, make the necessary preparations for themselves and not engage in useless actions that please the enemy.

Government Bonds: Principal Repayment Lottery Held Yesterday

Lottery Drawing: Three Bonds Repaid: Eight Hundred Thousand

Telecommunications Administration: Unified in Late June; Interest Paid in July

The first principal repayment and lottery drawing for the unified government bonds of the Republic of China, Class C and D, of 1936 and the third principal repayment lottery drawing for the telecommunications administration government bonds of 1935 were held at 10:00 AM yesterday on the fifth floor of the Banking Association. Present at the supervision were representatives of the Ministry of Finance Jiang Lvyin, Ministry of Communications Wen Yu, Audit Department Lin Jinyu, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Xu Jiquan, Banking Association Wu Weiruo, Native Bankers Association Shen Jingyun, Second Special District Local Court Hu Yuyin, Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce Luo Zong, National Debt Fund Custody Committee Fan Jietang, and lottery drawers Yuan of the Central Bank, Zhu Qizhen of the Bank of China, and Chen Jun of the Bank of Communications. The drawing was presided over by Jiang Keyi and involved drawing thirteen bonds in total, for a total principal repayment of four million eight hundred thousand yuan. The winning numbers are recorded below:

Chairman's Report: The chairman reported: "Today is the first principal repayment lottery drawing for the unified government bonds of the Republic of China, Class C and D, of 1936 and the second principal repayment lottery drawing for the telecommunications administration government bonds of 1935. The lottery method for the unified bonds uses the last digit of the bond number. The last number will be used. The details of each bond are reported as follows. The unified government bonds, Class C, of the Republic of China of 1936, were issued in February 1936, with a fixed amount of 350 million national currency. This is the first principal repayment lottery drawing for five bonds, each worth 350,000 yuan, for a total repayment of 1.75 million yuan. The unified government bonds, Class D, of the Republic of China of 1936, were issued in February 1936, with a fixed amount of 550 million national currency. This batch is the first principal repayment lottery drawing for five bonds, each worth 550,000 yuan, for a total repayment of 2.75 million yuan. The telecommunications administration government bonds of the Republic of China of 1935 were issued in the month of 1935, with a total amount of 10 million yuan. The principal has already been repaid twice. This is the third principal repayment lottery drawing for two bonds, each worth 100,000 yuan, for a total repayment of 300,000 yuan. The principal and matured interest of the above-mentioned winning bonds will be paid by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications in various locations, starting June 30 for the telecommunications administration government bonds and July 21 for the unified government bonds, Class C and D, by the Central Bank in various locations and its entrusted Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Central Trust Bureau. Furthermore, for the convenience of bondholders, the Ministry has agreed to allow the winning bonds of the unified government bonds, Class C and D, and the interest coupons maturing at the end of July to be rediscounted at the Central Bank or discounted at the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. This will be implemented and reported jointly after February 15, 1936. Now, we request the supervisors to inspect the lottery instruments and the lottery register in order to proceed with the lottery drawing."

Winning Numbers: Following the inspection of the lottery instruments and the register by the supervisors, the lottery drawing proceeded. Five bonds were drawn for the unified government bonds, Class C: No. 087, No. 149, No. 475, No. 588, and No. 839. Five bonds were drawn for the unified government bonds, Class D: No. 085, No. 470, No. 562, No. 845, and No. 977. Two bonds were drawn for the telecommunications administration government bonds: No. 09, No. 57, and No. 84.

The Amount of the Loan for Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Exceeds 10 Million

Number of Factories Increasing Loan Amounts, Etc.

The Silk Control Association Decides to Reel and Sell the Silk Themselves

The amount of the loan for the spring cocoon harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang in 1936, handled by the loan syndicate, has exceeded 10 million yuan. They are continuing to handle the increase in loan amounts. The Zhejiang Silk Control Association has decided to reel and sell the cocoons they have harvested themselves. After the release of the cocoons, various silk factories have successively started work. The details are recorded below:

The Loan Amount Exceeds 10 Million: The amount of the loan for the spring cocoon harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang in 1936, handled by the loan syndicate for silk manufacturers and cocoon merchants, has exceeded 10 million yuan as of yesterday, from the Shanghai General Office and the Hangzhou and Wuxi branch offices. Among these, Jiangsu accounts for eight-tenths, and Zhejiang accounts for two-tenths. To implement rural relief, the syndicate has decided to provide special accommodations. Even if applications are overdue, they will continue to handle the increase in loan amounts. The regular meetings of the standing committee member banks of the general and branch offices are still being held as usual. The date of the general meeting of the member banks has not yet been determined.

The Silk Control Association Reels and Sells the Silk Themselves: The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Association borrowed 5 million yuan from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications to organize the Spring Cocoon Harvest Committee of 1936. It has now been decided that the harvested cocoons will be distributed to various silk factories by the Silk Reeling Committee to reel silk with new-style silk reeling machines. After reeling, the Sales Committee will sell the silk to foreign markets, implementing self-reeling and self-selling. Furthermore, the Control Committee has received orders from the provincial government to release the cocoons of cocoon merchants who have charged prices below the standard, after retaining 40%. Samples are currently being tested to determine the method of disposal.

The Nanhua Shipping Line Reduces Its Number of Voyages and Suspends Sailings

Financial Impacts: Guangzhou Merchants Stop Loading Cargo

Shipping Declines: Crew Members Dismissed and Unemployed

In the past three days, due to the current situation, the price of the Guangdong currency has fallen to an unprecedented record. Sixteen or seventeen yuan of Guangdong currency are equivalent to ten Hong Kong dollars, a decrease of two-fifths compared to the normal price. The Guangzhou merchants in Shanghai, after receiving telegrams from Guangzhou, have stopped loading various purchased goods. Only essential items are being shipped. The difference between the Guangdong currency and the Shanghai currency is too great, and it will be difficult to sell the goods in Guangzhou. Yesterday, the Haizhen ship sailed with a rare lack of cargo. The Haiyuan ship was diverted to Qingdao. The cargo for the Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and Nanhua ships has also decreased sharply.

Taikoo Reduces Voyages: The British-owned Taikoo Company, located on Nanhua Road, has the largest presence. It originally had regular ships sailing to Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, and Haiphong, with five voyages per week on Mondays, Wednesdays, Thursdays, Fridays, and Saturdays. Temporary ships were not included. More than 45 regular Nanhua voyages were made each month. Recently, due to the decline in cargo and the decrease in business, the company has reduced the number of regular Nanhua voyages from Shanghai to two per week, changing the voyages to Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, reducing the number of voyages by about eight or nine per month.

Suspension of Voyages for Various Ships: The Taikoo Company had more than ten temporary ships sailing between Nanhua and Shanghai and also sailing to North China. Recently, due to a lack of cargo, the company decided to suspend the voyages of seven ships first. The Liangzhou and Yingzhou ships have already stopped sailing, and crew members have been dismissed. Now, due to a greater lack of cargo, the company has officially decided to suspend the voyages of various ships. The Zhejiang will officially stop sailing upon arrival in Shanghai today. The Luzhou and Chongqing are scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 13th for a break. The Chengdu will also come to Shanghai and stop sailing. Only the Ganzhou is still transporting coal in Haizhou and will also have to stop sailing soon.

Agricultural Loan Syndicate Increases Loans to Shanxi Province: Allocating from the Initial Total of 2.5 Million Yuan, Increasing the Total Amount at the Board Meeting When Necessary

The China Agricultural Cooperative Loan Syndicate's agricultural loan for the 1936 fiscal year was decided at the board meeting on the fifth of last month to be 2.5 million national currency. Of this amount, Jincheng and Jiaotong Banks each subscribed to 500,000 yuan, Shanghai Bank subscribed to 400,000 yuan, Zhejiang Xingye subscribed to 300,000 yuan, and Zhongnan, Dalu, and the Four Banks Savings Society each subscribed to 200,000 yuan, while Guohua and Xinhua each subscribed to 100,000 yuan. Now it is stipulated that 250,000 yuan will be used for production loans in Hebei Province, 250,000 yuan for production loans in Shaanxi Province, 500,000 yuan each for transportation and sales loans in Hebei and Shaanxi Provinces, and 1 million yuan for warehouse mortgage loans in Anhui Province. In addition to the Anhui warehouse mortgage loans, which will be jointly handled with the Bank of China and the Farmers Bank of China, it has now been decided to increase production, transportation, and sales loans to Shanxi Province by 400,000 yuan. This amount will first be allocated from the total of 2.5 million yuan. If necessary, the board meeting will be convened again to increase the total amount of loans for the 1936 fiscal year.

Guangdong Province: Cancellation of the Hemp Surtax Approved by the Southwest Political Affairs Committee

After the collection of a surtax of 2.5 jiao per dan on Guangdong hemp to fund the construction of Sun Yat-sen University, merchants of miscellaneous grains, bean cakes, and oil mills across the country went on strike and petitioned for the cancellation of the surtax. Subsequently, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee decided to reduce the surtax on domestic hemp to 1.5 jiao per dan. A reporter from the New Voice Society visited Mr. Gu Shengyi yesterday, who stated that the contract for the surtax on Guangdong hemp will expire at the end of August. The Southwest Political Affairs Committee has now decided to completely cancel the surtax on hemp from the end of August. However, the relevant associations have not yet received formal approval.

Two Domestic Goods Organizations Discuss Preventing Smuggling

The Shanghai Federation of Domestic Goods Factories previously sent letters to its members soliciting suggestions on how to address the rampant smuggling in North China, which was affecting the sales of domestic goods. The Federation has now received proposals from a majority of its members and will organize an anti-smuggling committee with the Chamber of Commerce, various trade associations, and national activist groups. The committee will investigate all factories and merchants and confiscate any smuggled goods. These smuggled goods will then be auctioned off at a reduced price, and the proceeds will be used for national defense construction. The Federation will submit these proposals to an executive committee meeting to be held this week for discussion. Additionally, the Federation of Machine-Made Domestic Goods Factories, responding to member demands to oppose the increase of troops in North China and smuggling, has decided to raise the issue at its upcoming general meeting to discuss concrete measures.

The Shanghai Leather Goods Trade Association held a general meeting yesterday afternoon, attended by more than 30 people. Song Zhongqing was sent by the Social Affairs Bureau for guidance. Subsequently, Chen Jiufeng, Li Mingde, and Liu Zhongying were elected as standing committee members, Chai Shunfu and Zhang Ruzhou as general managers, Tao Lianqing and Hu Meifu as financial officers, Jin Pinyou and Zhou Longzhang as investigators, and Wang Jian'e as the representative. The meeting also resolved the following:

* **Proposal to solicit ordinary and mandatory membership in the Trade Association:** It was decided to task Jin Pinyou, Hu Mei, Tao Liqing, and Zhou Longzhang with the responsibility of soliciting members. Industry regulations will be established once a majority of people have joined the association.

* **Proposal to standardize production and unify market prices:** It was resolved to adopt and implement the proposal in conjunction with the above proposal.

* **Discussion of employee benefits and standardization of wages:** It was resolved to discuss the matter after investigating the wages of various factories.

* **Proposal that rampant smuggling is related to the national economy and the people's livelihood and should be secretly investigated in cooperation with the government:** It was resolved to form a Leather Goods Trade Association Anti-Smuggling Association.

* **Proposal that Japan's increase in troops in North China hinders China's sovereignty and the government should ensure the integrity of sovereignty:** It was resolved to petition the central government for serious negotiations.

* **Proposal to seek the physical health of employees in the same industry and to uniformly join civil training:** It was resolved to notify the industry throughout the city to encourage employees to participate in civil training uniformly.

* **Proposal to telegraph the Central and Southwest Governments to stop the civil war:** It was resolved to pass the proposal, uphold peace and unity, and unite against foreign aggression.

Dutch East Indies Restricts Import of Native Cloth

The International Trade Bureau sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday regarding the Dutch East Indies' restriction on the import of Chinese native cloth. The letter stated that the Shanghai Native Cloth Trade Association had previously written to the Bureau, requesting that it forward letters to the Consulate in the Netherlands and the Commercial Commissioner to negotiate for the cancellation of the restriction on the import of native cloth. The Bureau had already forwarded letters to the Consulate in Batavia and the Commercial Commissioner in Semarang, requesting them to find ways to handle the matter, and had also submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry to consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct them to handle the matter. The Bureau had also replied to the Association. The Consulate General in Batavia replied with letter number 2688, stating that the Consulate had received letter number 627 from the Bureau, as well as a letter and several fabric samples from the Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Medan. The Consulate had submitted the case to the Director of the Import Bureau of the Department, requesting him to instruct all customs offices to allow the entry of overweight Chinese coarse cloth as usual, and had attached the fabric samples sent by the Medan Chamber of Commerce for inspection. The Director replied, stating that he had repeatedly allowed the import of special Chinese cotton cloth that exceeded the specified weight, and would consider the interests of the importers of these special Chinese cotton cloth as much as possible. However, he could not comply with the Consul General's request for a general allowance. Whether or not the import of cotton cloth exceeding the specified weight could be approved must be submitted for approval on a case-by-case basis. Importers who intend to import cotton cloth exceeding the specified weight must submit samples for inspection no later than when submitting the application requesting the issuance of the relevant permit. If the import permit for cotton cloth does not contain clauses regarding the specified quantity, the merchant only needs to send the permit to the customs for inspection when the goods are imported, and the goods can be released without hindrance. The Bureau has informed the Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Medan and is now forwarding copies of the correspondence between the Consulate and the Director to the Bureau for reference, hoping that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Native Cloth Trade Association will be informed for their reference.

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Notifies Stock Exchange Federation to Strictly Prohibit Brokers from Trading Off-Exchange, Orders Compliance with Law for All Transaction Records, Penalties for Brokers Who Disobey, Report to Ministry of Industry and Commerce

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, due to the inability of various stock exchanges in Shanghai to enforce the requirement for brokers to create transaction records in accordance with the law, which has led to a small number of profit-seeking brokers privately settling accounts off-exchange, undermining national taxes and disrupting the market, affecting social stability, notified the Stock Exchange Federation again to reiterate the previous order, strictly prohibiting such practices, and instructed them to inform all stock exchanges and brokers associations. The original text of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's notification is excerpted as follows: "Stock exchanges have the special privilege of managing the market. All transactions made by brokers or members in the market, from the time of transaction to the completion of settlement, are subject to the condition that they are effective through the stock exchange. The former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in the 18th year of the Republic (1929), received a report from the Federation stating that brokers were trading off-exchange and privately settling accounts, which was a clear violation of the law. The Ministry responded with Business Document No. 2444, stating that clients entrusting trades should request the stock exchange to stamp and certify all transactions made at any time, and that the stock exchanges themselves should strictly abide by the regulations and earnestly eliminate long-standing malpractices. After the implementation of the Stock Exchange Law, it was clearly stipulated in Article 29 of the implementing rules that the notification letter of brokers' buying, selling, and settling on the stock exchange would not be effective unless it was stamped and certified by the stock exchange. Last year, the amended Stock Exchange Law was promulgated, and Article 38, Paragraph 2, further stipulated that the transaction record should be created by the stock exchange and issued to both brokers for signature and completion. All these regulations are intended to ensure that all trades made by brokers are carried out through the stock exchange to obtain legal protection and avoid the malpractices of private transactions. It has now been found that the Shanghai stock exchanges often act perfunctorily towards the trades of each broker and do not enforce the requirement to create transaction records in accordance with the law. As a result, brokers seeking private gain can privately settle accounts outside the stock exchange and take advantage of short-selling, which not only erodes national taxes, stock exchange revenue, and transaction fees, but also affects the financial market and social stability. Such trading practices that do not comply with legal procedures should be strictly prohibited to maintain the law. In the future, all trades made by brokers on behalf of clients, whether buying, selling, or settling, must be carried out through the stock exchange to which they belong, and the transaction record must be created by the stock exchange in accordance with the law and issued to both brokers for signature and completion. If any broker violates this regulation or engages in private settlement and trading off-exchange, the stock exchange to which they belong shall impose penalties in accordance with the regulations and report the matter to the Ministry for verification. Stock exchanges should also manage the market and handle trading and settlement matters in accordance with laws and regulations, without any errors. In addition to instructing the Shanghai Stock Exchange Supervisor to supervise compliance at any time, this notification is hereby issued to the Federation, instructing it to inform all stock exchanges and brokers associations to comply and truthfully report the compliance to the Ministry for record. This is hereby notified. June 6, 25th year of the Republic of China (1936). Minister Wu Dingchang."

Fourth Son of Cen Chunxuan Accused of Cohabiting with a Dancer, Both Parties Have Reached an Out-of-Court Settlement, Court Rules Inadmissible

Cen Delin (also known as Shenxian), the fourth son of Cen Chunxuan, the former Governor-General of Liangguang and Chief Executive of the Southwest Military Government during the late Qing Dynasty, who married Ding Naixian, the sister of Ding Naiyang, the former Salt Commissioner of Lianghuai, cohabited with Zhang Ying (also known as Zhang Yin), a dancer at the Fuxing Shanghai Ballroom, in room 10 of the apartment building at No. 446 Seymour Road. After Ding discovered this, she reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate and found that Cen and Zhang were indeed cohabiting. She then filed a public prosecution with the First Special District Court on the charge of adultery under Article 239 of the Criminal Law. After hearing the case, the court ordered a postponement for further hearing. Within the postponement period, Cen and Zhang each paid bail to ensure their appearance as required, with a guarantee responsibility of no less than 10,000 yuan, ordering the two parties to reach a settlement out of court. Yesterday morning was the date for the continuation of the hearing. The plaintiff Ding Naixian and her attorney were not present, only the defendant's attorney appeared in court, stating that the two parties had reached a settlement out of court and that the plaintiff had submitted a statement withdrawing the charges. The judge then sent the plaintiff's statement of withdrawal to the police attorney Qian Xunjiu for review. Qian made no objection, and the judge declared the case inadmissible.

On the Relocation of Graves in Ning County, a Lawsuit Regarding the Abandonment of Corpses Has Been Filed: Gan Shi-xiong Sues His Brother and Nephew

After the death of Gan Chang-chun, the Ningbo native and owner of the Gan Fu Tai Woolen Shop on Broadway Road, he left behind a significant amount of property. It was immediately divided according to the law among his son, Gan Shi-tao, Gan Shi-xiong, and grandson, Yu Xue-ting, and others. A portion of the property was designated as ancestral property, with its income used for ancestral sacrifices. The three individuals would take turns managing it each year. The annual income from this ancestral property was approximately one thousand several hundred yuan. This year, it was Gan Shi-xiong's turn to manage it. Furthermore, due to the Ning County government's order that all graves in the urban area must be relocated, Gan Shi-xiong consulted with Gan Shi-tao and Gan Xue-ting about how to proceed and requested the ancestral property deeds be handed over. However, the two refused to hand them over and, on April 28th, Gan Shi-tao's wife, Zhang, evicted Gan Shi-xiong from her residence at No. 6 Houde Lane, Gansu Road. Consequently, Gan Shi-xiong filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against Gan Shi-tao, Gan Xue-ting, and Gan Zhang for abandoning corpses and obstructing the exercise of his rights. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shu-zi presided over the Third Criminal Court and summoned them for questioning. According to Gan Shi-xiong's testimony, on April 1st, due to the county government's order to relocate graves, he specifically consulted with the defendants. However, they all refused to take any action and refused to hand over the ancestral property deeds. On April 28th, when he went to Gan Shi-tao's house, his wife, Zhang, ordered two individuals who resembled gangsters to evict him, which is why he filed the lawsuit. Gan Shi-tao and Gan Xue-ting testified that this year was indeed the plaintiff's turn to manage the ancestral property, but he was deeply addicted to opium. The houses in Shanghai had been almost entirely sold off. If the ancestral property were handed over to him, it would inevitably be sold off. Therefore, it was specifically kept in the custody of the Shanghai Industrial Bank. As for the income from the ancestral property, he was free to collect it. Regarding the grave relocation matter, Gan Xue-ting had been to Ningbo several times, and the county government had now announced that old graves did not need to be relocated. Therefore, there was no need for further relocation. When questioned, Gan Zhang also denied instigating gangsters to evict the plaintiff. The court, having clarified the facts, ordered the start of the debate and then declared the conclusion of the hearing, setting a date for sentencing.

Compulsory Demolition of Rooms on Sun Decks in the Nine Acres Area; Police Hire Masons and Carpenters on Behalf of the Landlord; Tenants Suffer Significant Losses

The houses along the Nine Acres Area's Luxiangyuan Road were newly built last year by the Anhe Company. They are divided into five neighborhoods: Ren'an Lane, Yi'an Lane, Ji'an Lane, Zhi'an Lane, and Xin'an Lane, totaling over two hundred buildings. After the construction was completed, tenants successively opened businesses or residences. Recently, due to the sluggish market and planned economy, to reduce expenses, small rooms were added on the sun decks, or a small floor was added. Each household spent approximately two hundred yuan in legal tender. Recently, the Municipal Public Works Bureau discovered that adding rooms to completed buildings could be dangerous. They notified the Anhe Company to inform the tenants to demolish the additions by a deadline. However, all the tenants, feeling that the construction had been very costly, intended to petition the authorities for a postponement of the demolition. Unfortunately, the deadline had passed. Yesterday (Tuesday), the competent branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched numerous police officers, along with the landlord, to supervise a large number of masons and carpenters, etc., to forcibly demolish the additions in each neighborhood. Within half a day, the rooms built on the sun decks of hundreds of houses were completely demolished, and the tenants suffered significant losses.
