There are 730,000 Monks and Nuns Nationwide; The Number of Lay Buddhists Reaches Over 3 Million; Five Provinces Including Sichuan, Jiangxi, and Henan are Not Included

The number of temples, monks, nuns, and lay Buddhists (commonly known as those who practice with hair) in our country has never been statistically recorded. Even Buddhists themselves cannot give a definite answer. Last spring, the Chinese Buddhist Association sent letters to local branches to collect statistical materials on this matter. After compiling and submitting the tables, the association has now compiled the results. The figures are approximately as follows: There are over 267,000 large and small temples and nunneries nationwide (excluding the five provinces of Sichuan, Henan, Jiangxi, Anhui, and Hunan). The number of monks and nuns totals over 738,000. The number of lay Buddhists (i.e., devotees) is over 3,690,000, which is more than five times the number of monks and nuns.

The "Min Tuo" Ship Suffers Damage After Its Victory

The "Min Tuo" Suffers More Damage After the "Victory"

The "Min Tuo" of the Minsheng Company is a shallow-water riverboat that operates on the routes from Yichang to Chongqing and Shanghai to Chongqing. Recently, the bottom of the ship suffered minor damage and needed to undergo major repairs in dry dock. This time, the ship came from Chongqing to Shanghai to unload cargo and entered the Laogongmao Shipyard on the 9th for repairs. Unexpectedly, after the dry dock was filled with water and the gate was closed, the gate suddenly broke due to the force of the water. The water rushed downstream, causing the hull of the "Min Tuo" to be pushed and swing from side to side, resulting in it colliding with the stone wall inside the dry dock. The iron plates on the outer hull of the ship were all damaged, and it is said that the hull was also breached, causing flooding. After the accident, the Minsheng Company was immediately notified. Yesterday, the Maritime Affairs Bureau dispatched technicians to inspect the damage. Today, the water in the dry dock still needs to be drained to further inspect the bottom of the ship before estimating the damage and carrying out repairs.

The "Victory" Runs Aground on a Sandbar

The "Victory" of the Zhengji Company is a ship with a deadweight of 924 tons, a length of 215 feet, a width of 31 feet 3 inches, and a draft of 14 feet 6 inches. It can travel 9 nautical miles per hour. It originally sailed the Shanghai-Beiyang route. Recently, it loaded cargo in Dalian and headed to Japan. While sailing outside the entrance of Wakayama Port, it ran aground on a sandbar because the nautical chart did not have any record of a sandbar there. The captain of the "Victory" did not know about the sandbar and unfortunately ran aground. After the accident, the captain immediately telegraphed the Wakayama office, requesting that a tugboat be sent to rescue the ship as soon as possible, planning to tow it off the sandbar at high tide. The Shanghai company has also been notified.

The Yichang Pawnshop in Pudong Suffers a Major Theft; Thieves Climb a Four-Zhang-High Wall to Enter, Stealing Gold Jewelry and a Handgun

The Yichang Pawnshop in Laiyidu, Pudong, has a long history. It is surrounded by a thick wall four zhang in height. Suddenly, at midnight the day before yesterday, thieves broke in. They climbed up the wall using utility poles and wooden ladders, then descended using ropes. They entered the jewelry section in the west wing through a window above the door, opened boxes, and stole over sixty pieces of jewelry and gold ornaments, estimated to be worth over two thousand taels of gold, as well as a military handgun with serial number 2840. After completing the theft, they exited using the ropes. It was not discovered until dawn. The Pudong Branch Bureau and the Second Team of the Security Corps were notified to investigate the scene. Many fingerprints were found on the doors and windows, and the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Fingerprint Section was requested to send personnel to match the fingerprints in order to arrest the perpetrators.

A Tragic Fire on Rue Foch: Five Dead, Six Injured; The Fire Started in the Hexingchang Tire Repair Shop; A Month-Old Girl Burned to Death

Hexingchang, located at 370 Rue Foch (west of Chengdu Road), a shop repairing and selling automotive parts, caught fire suddenly at 2:30 AM yesterday. Because it was late at night, five people were burned to death and six were injured. The details are as follows:

Multiple Tenants: 370 Rue Foch is a single-bay lower-level house rented by Guo Benren from Ningbo. In addition to using the street level as a shop, the front building on the second floor was sublet to Feng Renlu (a traveling salesman) and his wife from Wuxi. The rear building was also sublet to Xi A'da (an automotive repairman) and his wife from Pudong. Xi's wife had given birth to a girl earlier this month. At the same time, a three-story loft was built upstairs and rented by Lu Qiaosheng, who worked as a tea server at the Southeast Hotel.

Five Fatalities: At 2:30 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the Hexingchang shop on the lower level. Because it was late at night, all the residents were fast asleep. By the time they realized what was happening, the fire had already spread rapidly. The stairs connecting the lower level to the second floor had been burned away, preventing Feng and his wife in the front building, Xi A'da's wife and newborn child in the rear building, and the shop owner Guo Benren's father-in-law (surnamed Li) from escaping. They were all burned to death in a terrible tragedy.

Fire Did Not Spread to Neighbors: Those who were burned on the head and face or injured after jumping from the building included Xi A'da, Lu Qiaosheng, Xi Lin'gen, Li Zhixiang, Hang Xiaolin, and Li Guo. The Xinzha Fire Brigade quickly arrived with five pump trucks and one ambulance, and the Tiantong Road Fire Brigade also arrived with one pump truck to help put out the fire. At the same time, the injured were transported to Binlong Hospital for treatment. By about 4:00 AM, the fire was extinguished, preventing it from spreading to neighboring buildings. The Chengdu Road Police Station immediately dispatched a large number of detectives to maintain order at the scene.

Court Inspection: During the removal of the five bodies (two men, two women, and one child), it was discovered that Xi A'da's wife was not yet dead, so she was taken to Guangren Hospital. However, she died soon after due to her severe injuries. The bodies were transported to the Forensic Examination Office on Fellen Road. At approximately 10:00 AM yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Song Gen-shan, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zu-ji, to inspect the bodies one by one to confirm their identities. Afterward, the detectives reported the situation and stated that the preliminary investigation suggested that the fire was caused by an electrical fault. Mr. Song then ruled that the deaths were caused by burns sustained in the fire. The bodies of Xi Zhang, Xi's daughter were released to Xi Zhiben, and the body of Li Litang was released to Guo Benshun. As the Feng family's relatives have not yet been identified, their bodies were delivered to the Pushan Cemetery pending claims.

The Wife of Painter Cheng Yao-sheng Accuses His Adopted Son of Embezzlement and Abandonment; The Case Involves Cheng Yao-sheng's Scandalous History; Due to Incorrect Citation of Laws, the Hearing is Postponed

Cheng Li Xiujin (age 50), the wife of the late famous painter Cheng Yao-sheng from Anhui, residing at No. 190 Temple Street in Xiaodongmen, Nanshi, Shanghai, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Second Special Court's Criminal Division against Cheng Yao-sheng's adopted son, Cheng Yin-sheng (age 35, residing in Taiping Bridge), and Rong-sheng (age 30, residing at No. 40 Tianzhutang Street, Yongqing Money Exchange), the son he had with a Wuxi maid, accusing them of embezzlement and abandonment. The plaintiff stated that when she was 17 years old, Yang Gui-sheng (a colleague of Yao-sheng), an employee of the Jihang Pawnshop in Changzhou, acted as matchmaker. In November of the same year, she married Cheng Yao-sheng at his residence at Muqiaotou in Changzhou. The following year, she gave birth to a son named Rongguan, who died shortly after birth. During this time, Yao-sheng's artistic talent became renowned, and he resigned from his pawnshop job to come to Shanghai with her, where he earned a considerable income from painting. Yao-sheng then indulged in pleasure, leading to a breakdown in the couple's relationship. He often beat the plaintiff. When the plaintiff was 33 years old, she became pregnant and was beaten, resulting in a miscarriage. While she was hospitalized, Yao-sheng had an affair with Dai, a maid he had hired from Wuxi. From then on, the maid usurped the plaintiff's position and colluded to abuse the plaintiff. They brought in the son the Wuxi maid, Dai, had given birth to, renamed him Rong-sheng, and raised him together. Unable to endure the abuse, the plaintiff went to Guangfu Temple in Changzhou, where she recited scriptures day and night, resigned to her fate. By 1934, the plaintiff's private savings had been exhausted, and her supplies were cut off, leading to a lawsuit. After mediation by friends and relatives, Yao-sheng paid her 1,500 yuan as temporary living expenses. Unexpectedly, Yao-sheng passed away on March 15th of this year. The first defendant, Yin-sheng, and the second defendant, Rong-sheng, colluded to not notify the plaintiff and embezzled all of Yao-sheng's assets worth over ten thousand yuan and abandoned the plaintiff. She requested that the court investigate and prosecute them according to the law and also filed a civil lawsuit to recover living expenses. Based on the lawsuit, the court summoned the parties to the Second Criminal Court yesterday morning, with Judge Sun Peng-xian presiding. First, the plaintiff, Cheng Li Xiujin, recounted the events. The first defendant, Cheng Yin-sheng, testified that he did not know the plaintiff. The second defendant was represented by a lawyer, who submitted a defense and filed a counterclaim for false accusation. The lawyer stated that Yao-sheng had passed away and that the will named the defendant as the legal heir. There was also an elderly mother, Cheng Dai, and the plaintiff was not mentioned. Furthermore, the lawyer stated that the deceased father's documents included a receipt signed by the plaintiff on December 22, 1934, stating that due to her poverty, she had received 1,500 yuan in national currency from her late husband out of compassion, and that she would never make any further requests. There was also no record of a marriage in Changzhou. After reviewing the lawsuits from both sides, the court determined that the plaintiff had cited the wrong criminal law articles in her lawsuit. Therefore, the hearing was postponed, and the plaintiff was instructed to correct the lawsuit before a new hearing date would be scheduled.

Zhu Wenbao Borrows Ancient Silver to Deceive a Foolish Woman; He Knocks Off a Corner of the Silver and Melts It to Cash In; Relatives Discover It is Fake

Lu Zhao, a woman residing at No. 569 Kang Nao Tuo Road, West Shanghai, filed a lawsuit with the District Court accusing Zhu Wenbao of fraud, stating that the defendant brought her three silver ingots in March of the previous year, each weighing one hundred taels. He falsely claimed that a villager had unearthed hundreds of ancient silver ingots, but he was afraid of being reported and could not exchange them all at once. Each ingot was worth about one hundred and several tens of yuan, and if she could buy them, she would make a great profit. At first, she was hesitant and undecided. The defendant then knocked off a corner of the silver ingot on the spot, melted it, and asked her to take it to a silver shop to exchange it. It was said that she exchanged it for one yuan and forty cents, proving that it was genuine silver. The plaintiff believed it was true and handed over 150 yuan as the price of the three ingots for the time being. Cao Dai was present at the scene and witnessed the transaction. The defendant also said that the purchase of the silver ingots should not be disclosed to outsiders, otherwise, they might be confiscated by the authorities. After a short period of time, he would find a way to exchange them for cash. The plaintiff then hid the silver ingots in a secret place. Recently, she heard that possessing silver was against the law, so she negotiated with the defendant to exchange them for cash, but he kept postponing it. When her relatives found out about it, they examined the silver and discovered that it was fake. When she confronted the defendant, he threatened her. She originally intended to hand him over to the Public Security Bureau, but he had a lot of influence in the Caojiadu area and had many followers. She feared that she would fail and suffer harm instead. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit for investigation and prosecution. Judge Tang summoned the defendant for questioning yesterday. Zhu stated that he was also deceived. The judge ordered him to be released and to investigate and verify the facts.

Achievements of the Disputes Mediation Office of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society: Resolving Difficulties, Pacifying Matters, Weighing Emotions and Reasons, Maintaining a Fair Attitude

The Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society has over 40,000 registered rickshaw pullers as members. With such a large number of members, most of whom are laborers with limited knowledge, disputes often arise in their daily interactions. Moreover, their occupational environment involves constant contact with the outside world, whether they are running through the streets and unexpectedly encountering accidents, or embroiled in wage disputes that escalate into violent brawls. Before the establishment of the Mutual Aid Society, rickshaw pullers facing such incidents were often forced by their status and economic circumstances to endure unfair resolutions, even when they were in the right. At this time, the Mutual Aid Society's banner of protecting rickshaw pullers became the only reliable place for these rickshaw pullers to seek justice. Therefore, weighing emotions and reasons, resolving difficulties, and pacifying disputes became a considerable challenge for the responsible personnel of the association. Currently, the responsibility for handling such matters rests with the Disputes Mediation Office of the association. Since its establishment, the office has accepted and satisfactorily resolved approximately over two thousand cases, with compensation amounts ranging from a minimum of half a yuan to a maximum of 360 yuan. These cases include disputes between rickshaw pullers, disputes between rickshaw pullers and contractors, disputes between rickshaw pullers and police officers, and collisions between automobiles and rickshaws. After accepting such cases, the Mediation Office truly strives to handle them with utmost effort. Its attitude is always fair, its procedures are simple and swift, and its consideration of circumstances and application of reason are accurate and cautious. What is particularly commendable is that although the association's main purpose is to protect rickshaw pullers, it never favors them. It maintains complete impartiality in determining who is right and who is wrong. As a result, even though it never forces anyone to comply, most parties leave satisfied. Even when disputes arise between rickshaw pullers and rickshaw owners or contractors, those who accept mediation harbor no resentment. Furthermore, the ultimate goal of the office in handling these cases is to pacify the situation. Unless the circumstances are serious and there is no other option, it never easily resorts to legal procedures. The fact that all over two thousand dispute cases have been resolved satisfactorily in the Disputes Mediation Office, with only one or two out of every hundred cases being transferred to legal counsel, speaks volumes.

Unexpectedly, Li asked Tang to write a letter on the 2nd of this month to Wang Tiangao (i.e., Wang Lao Jiu), the owner of a timber business in Pudong, demanding 100 yuan, saying that if he did not give the money, he would be reported as an accomplice in the robbery. Yesterday, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. Police Lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the case and prosecuted according to Article 346 of the Criminal Law. According to the plaintiff Wang Tiangao, he had known Zhang Genbao (i.e., Li Jinsheng) for more than ten years, and he had repeatedly refused to lend him money. He said that businessmen have legitimate businesses and dare not associate with thieves. When questioned, Li and Tang confessed that Wang had planned and discussed the robbery case at Jiangjiaqiao on March 7th in the Liang'an Apartment, and that he had also said that if there was any trouble, he could find a way to help. Suspect Xu Hexiang Gave the Gun in the Zhoujiazui Road Robbery Case

On the 28th of last month, at 8:00 PM, four bandits suddenly came to the home of Zhang Ziren, a native of Suzhou, at No. 69, Lane 850, Zhoujiazui Road, and threatened them with guns, prohibiting them from making any noise. They robbed the family of valuables worth 100 yuan and fled in different directions. Cai Liu, the Chinese detective chief of the Huishan Police, and detectives Sun Shaqiong and Dong Fugen rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm and arrested two thieves, Fang Amao from Pudong and Qian Baobao from Shanghai. Fang was shot in the back while resisting and was taken to the police hospital along with a five-inch Browning pistol loaded with live ammunition. Qian confessed that the gun was owned by Xu Hexiang, a native of Shanghai who worked as a machine engineer at the 31st Printing Factory at No. 797, Kunming Road. The detectives then went to his home at No. 112, Huasheng Road, and arrested Xu, who was taken to the First Special District Court. Xu completely denied providing the gun and claimed that he did not know Fang Amao. It was ordered that Xu be detained until Fang recovered from his injuries for further investigation. Yesterday morning, the police sent Fang and Qian, along with the suspect Xu Hexiang, to the Third Criminal Court. According to Fang Amao's confession, he went to commit the robbery with Xu Afa, Zhang Agen, and Qian Baobao, who were still at large. Zhang Agen came up with the idea, and Zhang and Xu took the stolen goods. The gun was borrowed from Xu by Zhang at that time. The court questioned Fang, "You previously admitted at the police station that the gun was picked up by the volunteer army during the January 28th Incident. Why is your confession contradictory?" Fang said that his previous statement was false. When questioned, Qian insisted that Xu had indeed given him the gun. (It was found that Qian had also committed a robbery case before and had been sentenced to 15 years, but was released in a general amnesty.) Xu Hexiang confessed that they were completely framing him because their business introduction had failed. Although he had a four-inch small pistol for self-defense, licensed by the Public Works Department, he had returned it two years ago. Acting lawyer Wu Linkun stated that when the victim's family was robbed, he was working in the factory and had been invited to dinner by the Erh Lai Company at the Tongxinglou Restaurant. His colleague Zhu, a foreman, could testify. According to Zhu Deyuan, Xu Hexiang was indeed at the factory at that time and did not leave. He did have a gun before, which was licensed by the police department for self-defense. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered that the police investigate the case further and check Xu Hexiang's previously licensed self-defense gun's size and number, and the date his license was revoked before further investigation. All the defendants were returned to custody.

The Silk Weaving and Embroidery Industry in Shanghai (Continued)

— Compiled by China Credit Information

(Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, No. 27)

A Glimpse of Sales: The sales of woven products cover both domestic and foreign markets. At its peak, the annual trade volume was about 10 million taels. In the domestic market, in addition to Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the provinces of Pingjin and Northeast were the largest markets, accounting for almost half of the total amount. After the Shenyang Incident, the market was seized, the relationship increased, transportation and sales became difficult, and business plummeted by more than half, with only more than 2 million yuan per year.

After the late Qing Dynasty, there were also some exports to foreign countries, which were praised by Europeans and Americans and were happy to purchase. The annual export value was more than 3 million taels. It is reported that the exported embroidery products were mainly embroidered pillows, embroidered cushions, table cloths, and figures and scenery, and brocade and embroidered clothes were also welcome, as they were needed by people in foreign countries for historical costume dances. Qing Dynasty official robes were originally very delicate, and Westerners used them to make handbags, which were beautiful and practical. It is said that they have been almost completely collected in recent years. In addition, due to the global economic collapse, foreign sales have sharply decreased, with an annual value of only 100,000 to 1 million yuan in national currency, a decrease of 70% to 80% compared with 20 years ago.

Business Investigation: There were more than 100 embroidery businesses in Shanghai at the peak of their prosperity, with considerable profits. However, in the past ten years, disasters have occurred frequently, economic bankruptcy has occurred, and the market has become increasingly depressed. Business has plummeted, making it impossible to maintain operations, and many businesses have announced their closure or switched to other industries as a sideline. According to investigations, there are currently about 70 embroidery businesses, mainly engaged in embroidered screens, embroidered pillows, embroidered clothes, lace, tablecloths, and table covers. In addition to special operations, other embroidery products have generally become art decorations, and few people buy them. The following is a report on the larger ones:

Wan Li Yuan Gu Embroidery Shop, 98 Shanxi Road, Manager Liu Buyun; Mei Hua Art Company, 91 Shanxi Road, Manager Xu Baoxian; Rui Chang Xiang Embroidery Shop, 78 Shanxi Road; De Hua Su Embroidery Shop, 88 Shanxi Road, Manager Zou Jun; Zhou Fu Ji, 109 Shanxi Road, Manager Zhou Shangbin; Da Zhang Tai Gu Embroidery Shop, 283 Guangdong Road, Branch Shop 80 Shanxi Road; Xin Tai Xiang Gu Embroidery Shop, 110 Shanxi Road; Mei Zhang Gu Embroidery Shop, 87 Shanxi Road, Manager Dian Jun; Wan Yuan Xiang Embroidery Shop, 411 Hankou Road; Jin Hua Li Xiang Embroidery Shop, 405 Hankou Road; Xin Feng Business, 10 Lane 27 Hankou Road, Manager He Dahong; Mei Hua Embroidery Company, 40 Broadway, Manager Qiu Menghua; Cheng Chang Company, 119 Broadway, Manager Lin Yinmao; Cheng Kang Company, 18 Broadway, Manager Li Zexiang; Yu Ji Company, 28 Broadway, Manager Huang Xilong; Xie Long Company, 78 Broadway; Wen Sheng Embroidery Company, 648 Broadway, Manager Zhu Zhongqi; Chaozhou Company, 32 Lane 172 Kunshan Road; Mei Xing Company, 113 Central Building, Sichuan Road, Manager Sun Lengmang; Tian Ji Embroidery Company, 6 Lane 315 Xiafei Road; Qian Yuan Embroidery Company, 4 Jixiang Lane, Wanza Road; Yu Chang Pillow Embroidery Shop, 337 Yangshupu Road; De Chang Embroidery Company, 248 Yao Shengjiao Road, Manager Wang Xiangfu; Dai Zhufu, 158 Yao Zhujiao Road, Manager Dai Zhufu; Hua Embroidery Company, 222 North Suzhou Road; Yuan Li Gu Embroidery Shop, 12 Lane 449 Beijing Road; Tian Cheng Yong Embroidery Shop, 6 Lane 2 Beijing Road; Du Jinsheng Silk Weaving Factory, 811 North Sichuan Road, Manager Du Jinsheng, Branch Shop 471 Hankou Road; Qi Wen Art Silk Weaving Factory, Penglukou, North Sichuan Road, Manager Ma Bin; Guo Hua Art Silk Weaving Factory, Zhaofuli, Hankou Road, Manager Luo Lican; West Lake Art Silk Weaving Factory, Furniture Department Agency of Sincere Company, Manager Luo Yixian; Xing Ye Art Silk Weaving Factory (Hangzhou), Manager Hu Banghan; Rong Cheng Silk Weaving Factory, Liuying Road, Zhabei. It is found that among the above-mentioned merchants, except for a few who operate wholesale alone, 70% to 80% are engaged in retail and wholesale. As for foreign merchants engaged in export, they are agents and transfer wholesale customers to Chinese merchants.

Overview of Embroidery Workers: Embroidery is a hand-made industry for women, so all embroidered items rely on women's short needle weaving to be completed. Therefore, the relationship between embroidery shops and embroidery workers is very close, but there are very few long-term hires. They are mostly issued and priced at any time. Moreover, embroidery workers are mostly women from towns and villages, except for a small number of women from the middle and lower classes in cities who do embroidery at home. It is because their lives are simple and their wages are low. It is said that in Suzhou, Changsha, Wenzhou, Shantou and other places, in addition to farming or going out to do business, women in the countryside do needlework at home. It is estimated that there are 30,000 to 40,000 people, and the daily embroidery income is enough to provide food and clothing. Moreover, those with high skills can still have savings. Therefore, there are not a few men who do not engage in proper business and rely on women at home for childbirth. In recent years, due to rural bankruptcy and the collapse of the social economy, the embroidery industry has plummeted. Embroidery shops have closed down, work has been reduced, and tens of thousands of female workers have nothing to live on. Even those who are lucky enough to get work are competing with each other, tending to fall in price and squeeze each other, resulting in poor export products and difficulty in marketing. Therefore, the embroidery industry is getting worse and worse.

Criticism of Athletics Selection: Ma John Issues Statement; Athletics Representatives Train at Shen Garden Today; Song Junfu Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday and Makes Speech

Our country's World Games athletics team was formed the day before yesterday. The athletics head coach, Ma John, designated them to start their final training before going abroad at 4:00 PM today. Ma Makes Statement on Selection

There has been much dissatisfaction from all walks of life regarding this World Games preliminary selection. Yesterday, a reporter from Guoguang News Agency met with Mr. Ma John at De Lin Apartment. According to the conversation, there has been a lot of dissatisfaction from the outside world regarding this selection. I will humbly accept any mistakes, but I absolutely cannot admit that it was unfair. Also, because the number of representatives attending is limited, the selection committee members spent a lot of time deliberating during the selection process. For example, regarding the selection of decathlon representative Zhang Lingjia, the outside world believes that the selection was inappropriate. However, Zhang has a very good spirit of hard work and has a good understanding of psychology. Our country's participation in the World Games this time is mainly for observation, and participating in the decathlon will be more beneficial. Also, Zhang has decided to serve the sports community after returning to China, so he was selected this time. As for the selection of other representatives, they also have their own special strengths and advantages. In short, there was absolutely no favoritism in this selection. As for the participation of each representative in the World Games, they will participate in a maximum of two events. According to my observation, our country's 4x100m relay has a good chance of winning, and it has been decided that the four representatives Liu, Dai, Jia, and Fu will participate. The four are quite evenly matched in strength. Mr. Ma continued that he will convene a meeting of representatives this morning, and Song Junfu, Xia Xiang, and others will give instructions.

Song and Xia Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday

Song Junfu, the coach and manager of our World Games athletics team, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at about 2:00 PM on the Shun Da Wheel from Qingdao, especially for the training of the World Games representatives, which will begin today. Xia Xiang also rushed to Shanghai from his hometown of Danyang yesterday. Both are staying at De Lin Apartment. According to Mr. Song's conversation with a reporter from Guoguang News Agency, he is quite satisfied with the results of this athletics preliminary selection. Because training must begin tomorrow (i.e., today), I came from Qingdao to assist in everything. After the closing ceremony of the World Games, I will go to Europe and the United States with Mr. Ma John and Dong Shouyi to conduct inspections for reference. However, my vacation is not as long as Mr. Ma's, and I may return to China first.

Our Country's World Games Soccer Team

— Random Notes from a Trip to Europe, Written and Sent by Li Huitang

Suffering in the Longsi Car Compartment

After the Xinglong selection battle yesterday, the army moved to Surabaya again this morning (May 20). After breakfast at 6:00 AM, the train started at 7:00 AM. Longsi is about 400 kilometers apart, and the train took 11 hours to arrive. Riding a train in the tropical zone, under the scorching heat, crouching all day is the most painful thing. There is a lot of coal dust, and even if there is a breeze, it is still hot. We were extremely tired after the game yesterday, and today we suffered even more from the train ride, which was like adding frost to snow. What I saw in the car compartment was that the fields on both sides were connected, and the ridges were endless. The Dutch have special skills in water conservancy and irrigation, and the land here is fertile, so the agricultural products are abundant, which is unmatched by other places. Sometimes, in the small streams shaded by green trees, I can catch a glimpse of village women bathing and having fun in the natural bathroom without any cover. Don't laugh at the Malay village women, they are naturally raised, and their bodies are much healthier than our country's women. I remember when Nanhua toured the South a few years ago, Secretary Zeng Jun Jinghou had a poem saying, "Farm women are full of charm, Wearing light gauze to watch painted skirts, Borrowing a bit of white from pear blossoms, Their delicate posture is envied by those leaning on the building." From this, it can be seen that Malay women have their own moving charm. Every time the train arrives at a station, hawkers carry food on their heads and shout for sale. The prices of train food are extremely high. For the sake of economy, we all scramble to trade with the hawkers. The boredom of the whole day was finally spent in a state of half-awake and half-asleep fatigue. When I arrived at Surabaya Station, I saw thousands of lights. Those who came to greet us at the station were the staff of the Chinese Sports Association of the host and many representatives of overseas Chinese groups. I drove to the Ping An Ju Hotel to settle down. Twenty or so dirty bodies scrambled to take a bath. According to the order table, our team has three games in Surabaya. Surabaya is the largest market in Java, and its prosperity is no less than that of Batavia. The sugar industry relies on it for profits. We had a hard bath after the Sino-Japanese war, and after dinner, we rested in our residence and did not go out again.

Surabaya's First Battle: A Great Victory Over the Local Selection Team

Yesterday's train ride was hot and boring, and I slept soundly all night. This morning, the red sun was high in the sky, and many friends were still sleeping soundly. At 5:00 PM today (May 21), we made contact with the local selection team here. There were few spectators on this day, far less lively than in Balong. After 70 minutes, our team launched a swift attack and defeated the enemy team with a large score of 10 to 2, leaving no armor behind. The reasons why our team was able to achieve such outstanding results are: first, the strength of the other side was mediocre; second, the ball field was flat and soft, which was very conducive to our team's combat, unlike the ball field in Ruilong, which was troublesome and restricted movements, and all flexibility was lost; third, each member's performance was more improved. If it were not for the perfunctory work in the second half, the number of victories would not have been limited to this. The ball skills are quite similar to those of the Vietnamese in Saigon, but unfortunately their strength is insufficient. They will show their poverty at the end of the game, and they will not be able to cope with the situation. We can do whatever we want. Because the strength is very different in this game, the battle situation is not tense. The result was 10 to 2. Huang Yi Bao replaced Huang Jiliang as goalkeeper in the second half. Those who made contributions were Huitang, Jinshun three, and Shuiyi two. The players who responded to our team were on the left:

Huang Jiliang Huang Jiliang Tan Jiangbo Mai Shaohan Li Guowei Xu Yahui Liang Shutang Zheng Jiliang Li Huitang Feng Jingxiang Sun Jinshun Yang Shuiyi

The Ministry of Education Announces Regulations for Vocational School Advisory Committees

The Ministry of Education has announced the following regulations for establishing advisory committees in vocational schools: 1. Each vocational school, in order to improve training efficiency and meet practical needs, should establish an advisory committee in accordance with the provisions of these regulations. 2. The advisory committee shall be composed of five to seven experts or leaders from the agricultural, industrial, and commercial sectors of the same nature as the school, hired by the school. 3. When the advisory committee holds a meeting, the principal, mayor, and heads of moral education, academic affairs, and practical training shall all attend. 4. Members of the advisory committee are all honorary positions, but travel expenses may be provided for attending meetings. 5. The advisory committee shall meet once every three months. When necessary, the principal may convene an ad hoc meeting. 6. The tasks of the advisory committee are as follows: Matters related to the students' service ethics and spiritual training; Matters related to the review and selection of vocational subject materials; Matters related to the guidance and liaison of students' on-campus and off-campus practice; Suggestions on other school facilities. 7. If there are vocational schools of the same nature near each school, they may jointly organize an advisory committee, and the number of committee members may be appropriately increased. 8. The matters resolved by the advisory committee shall be implemented by the principal at his discretion. 9. These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Ministry of Education.

Dr. Yu Songyun Speaks on Midwifery Education

Mr. Yu Songyun, the principal of the Shanghai-German Midwifery School in this city, was previously dispatched by the Central and Jiangsu Provincial Governments to inspect medical administration and health education in European and American countries. He has now completed his mission and returned to the country. The faculty, staff, and students of the school, along with all the doctors and staff of the Shanghai-German Hospital, held a welcome meeting in the school's auditorium at 8 PM the other day, and invited Mr. Yu to speak about his inspection. He said, roughly: The medical and health education in our country has not yet reached a fully developed stage. If we want to improve and develop it, we should investigate the current situation in advanced European and American countries to learn from them. This time, I was dispatched by the government, but I believe that midwifery is directly related to the people's birthrate and is crucial. Therefore, for the development of the school and the hospital, I paid special attention to it. Now I will tell you about the midwifery education in various countries. Among the European countries, Germany, Austria, and Sweden are the most developed in midwifery education. The age of admission is between 20 and 35 years old. In terms of admission qualifications, Germany and Austria require junior high school graduation or nursing graduation, and then be recommended by other institutions. Sweden only requires junior high school graduation. The length of study is two years in Germany and Austria, and 23 months in Sweden. During the study period in Germany and Austria, in addition to attending the required courses, each person must deliver more than 80 babies under the guidance of a chief midwife before participating in the graduation examination. In Sweden, one must deliver 100 babies before participating in the graduation examination. As for the curriculum, Germany and Austria used to teach forceps delivery and inversion, but these operations are now prohibited, and they are not allowed to inject oxytocin or hemostatic agents. Any pathological changes must be handled by a doctor. Sweden does not prohibit the use of forceps delivery and inversion. In summary, because Germany and Austria have a surplus of doctors, the powers of midwives are strictly restricted, but the government is still working hard to promote it and fully guarantee their status. The situation in Sweden is exactly the same as in our country, and the midwifery industry is actively developing. Sweden has a population of more than 6,142,000 people, and there are only 3,000 midwives, which is not enough. Therefore, they are still actively trying to increase it. Our country has a population of more than 450 million people, and there are only more than 2,000 midwives, which is even more lacking than Sweden. Therefore, in my opinion, the future and status of a midwife is more promising among women's occupations in our country. Then Mr. Yu presented four points of the school's improvement plan: To sign agreements with public and private medical and health institutions in this city to provide students with internship opportunities; To organize a youth service corps to consolidate the spirit of cooperation between teachers and students; To select the best parts of the curriculum from the investigation of various countries and incorporate them into the teaching materials to enrich students' knowledge; The school has been repeatedly praised by the Ministry of Education and the Bureau of Education for sending personnel to investigate, finding that the faculty is well-prepared, the equipment is complete, the school building is suitable, and the internship is rich. The school is flattered and will continue to do its best to enrich the content and strive to be a national model. Then the students performed a new drama, and the meeting ended happily.

Shi Chongpeng's "Notes on Appreciating Famous Paintings" Published

The famous painter Shi Chongpeng has written a book entitled "Notes on Appreciating Famous Paintings" based on the paintings from our country's participation in the London Chinese Art Exhibition. It has now been beautifully printed and published by the Commercial Press, priced at 1.20 yuan per copy. The content is rich, divided into six chapters. The three Tang paintings, two paintings from the Five Dynasties, fifty-six Song paintings, thirty-nine Yuan paintings, forty Ming paintings, and thirty-eight Qing paintings are all criticized, and the schools, origins, residences, official positions, and salaries of famous artists of past dynasties are all researched. It is beneficial to our country's painting history, and it is not shallow. Each chapter is attached with film images of representative works, which are especially valuable, such as Li Zhaodao's "Spring Mountain Journey Picture" of the Tang Dynasty, "Snow Fishing Picture" of the Five Dynasties, Dong Beiyuan's "Dragon Lodging Suburban People Picture" of the Song Dynasty, Guo Xi's "Landscape Picture with Colors," Emperor Huizong's "Red Reed White Crane Picture," Li Di's "Two Herdsmen Returning Picture," Su Yingchen's "Autumn Garden Children Playing Picture," Yan Cipeng's "Four Happiness Picture," Xia Gui's "West Lake Willow Boat Picture," Lu Zonggui's "Spring Shao Mingxi Picture," "Song People's Loquat Monkey Picture," "Song People's Rich Flower Cat Picture," Qian Xuan's "Autumn Melon Picture" of the Yuan Dynasty, Cao Zhibai's "Double Pine Picture," Wu Zhen's "Bamboo Stone Picture," Wang Menggu's "Spring Ploughing Picture," Ni Zan's "Rongxi Qi Picture," Fang Congyi's "Gaogao Pavilion Picture," Shen Shitian's "Lushan Gao Picture" of the Ming Dynasty, Lu Ji's "Apricot Flower Peacock Picture," Tang Bohu's "Mountain Road Pine Mushroom Picture," Qiu Ying's "Autumn River Waiting Ferry Picture," Dong Qichang's "Summer Wood Hanging Yin Picture," Wang Lianzhou's "Smoke Floating Distant Mountains Picture" of the Qing Dynasty, Chen Hongshou's "Rolled Stone Camellia Wang Shigujiang Village Xia Xia Tu", Wang Wu's "Flower and Bird Picture," Shi Tao and Luntai's collaborative "Orchid Bamboo Picture," and other twenty-eight frames, which are exquisite and wonderful, and are very worthy of appreciation.

Finance: Although Raw Gold Shrinks, Speculation Buying is Strong

—Reflection of People's Mindset—

Although raw gold shrank yesterday, due to the current situation, it made the buying from large households strong. The foreign exchange market tightened, with demand exceeding supply and prices rising. The swap spread is narrow. The future is extremely difficult to determine. In the early morning, it was said that the overseas silver market, with the English market shrinking and the American market at the same level, and the big dealers said that after the market closed, there were a few Indian buyers above the listed price of 0.0625, and finally there were buyers at the listed price, and the sellers were at a loss. Forward silver prices fell 2.7 to 4.5 fen. Exchange rates all rose. London raw gold fell 4 pence. The Central Bank's listing was announced, with the English and American markets both flat. The customs gold unit shrank 4 li, and the standard gold price listing fell to 1,130 yuan. Over-the-counter forward trading opened at 40 yuan and 5 jiao. Chunyuan, Yonghui Xiang, Dadecheng, Futai, Yong and others bought, rising to more than 1 yuan and 5 jiao. Fuxing Yongda Decheng slightly sold, and slightly挫 (frustrated). The opening in the morning was slightly higher, and the situation after the opening was confused, and it once turned weak. However, due to large households taking advantage of the low prices to buy, it was able to maintain. After the HSBC listing was flat, the silver balance tax shrank by 1.25 fen, but it had little impact. The buying from large households turned strong, and the forward foreign exchange market tightened even more, gradually rising. However, due to multiple parties closing out at high prices, it once挫 (fell). However, the surface was more涸 (dry), and the demand side was easily激 (agitated) and动 (moved). 1935 Annual Silk Export Report

Export Volume Increases... Unfortunately, Quality Deteriorates

Eliminate Inferior Silk Exports... Implemented on July 1

According to the silk export report of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, the total export of Shanghai raw silk in 1935 was 56,025 bales, an increase of 32,095 bales compared to last year, accounting for 13.40 percent. Among them, the export increase of white factory silk was the largest, accounting for 27,097 bales, followed by Zhili silk, with an increase of 2,526 bales, and then white soil silk, with an increase of 1,061 bales. The increase in yellow silk and others was relatively small. In terms of export locations, the Americas accounted for the most, with an increase of 18,402 bales compared to last year, followed by Europe, with an increase of 10,143 bales. In short, the raw silk export trade showed signs of turning from adversity to prosperity in 1935. However, it is heard that amidst this recovery of the silk industry, the raw silk exported from our country has been criticized by the international market due to its deteriorating quality, which is regrettable. Recently, the Ministry of Industry decided to implement quality inspection of exported raw silk to eliminate the export of poorly made raw silk and improve the overseas reputation of Chinese silk. It has ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to actively prepare and implement it on July 1 of this year. This is indeed an essential measure for the foreign trade of raw silk, and it is also a new opportunity for silk manufacturers to follow and strive for.

Popular Lecture

Wang Xie

- Su Zihan

The states during the Warring States period were all fighting for each other, and there was almost war every year. If two countries had a feud, then the war would never end.

At that time, King Min of Qi was immoral, and he was very tyrannical to his officials and people. He also wanted to become emperor and divide the world equally with the Qin state. When King Min of Qi called himself the Eastern Emperor, it was when King Kuai of Yan ceded the throne to Chancellor Zi Zhi. There was civil strife in the Yan state, and King Min of Qi took advantage of this opportunity to lead troops to attack the Yan state. The Yan state had been messed up by King Kuai of Yan and Zi Zhi, the soldiers did not want to fight, and the people did not want to defend the city. When the Qi soldiers came, they were unstoppable and occupied many cities. King Kuai of Yan was killed in battle, and Zi Zhi ran away, but he did not escape in the end. He was captured by the Qi army and minced into meat sauce. The remaining people of the Yan state established King Kuai of Yan's crown prince as king, who was King Zhao of Yan.

After King Zhao of Yan ascended the throne, he always remembered the hatred of King Min of Qi for killing his father and attacking his country. He always thought, "King Min of Qi is too unreasonable. He took advantage of the civil strife in my country to attack my country, kill my father, and occupy many cities. This revenge must be avenged. However, the Yan state is too small, and after a new defeat, if I want to recover, I must hire virtuous people from all over the world to do this work of saving the country."

Therefore, King Zhao of Yan treated virtuous people with courtesy, respected Guo Wei as a teacher, and repaired a house for Guo Wei to live in. The virtuous people of the world all knew that King Zhao of Yan was treating virtuous people with courtesy, wanting to avenge the country and avenge the national humiliation. Most of the virtuous people of the world went to the Yan state, such as Yue Yi from the Wei state, Zou Yan from the Qi state, and Ju Xin to the Zhao state.

In this way, more than twenty years passed. During these more than twenty years, King Zhao of Yan was very attentive to national affairs and not at all careless. He treated the people well and the soldiers well. It can truly be said that he shared weal and woe with the people and soldiers. King Zhao of Yan also appointed some virtuous people to manage all production undertakings and the undertakings of enriching the country and strengthening the army, and they managed them very well. The Yan state then became strong. In the twenty-eighth year of King Zhao of Yan, which was the fortieth year of King Min of Qi, King Zhao of Yan ordered Yue Yi to be the supreme general, uniting the troops of various countries to attack the Qi state, killing the Qi state's troops and horses and defeating them greatly. The troops of various countries returned, and Yue Yi led the troops of the Yan state alone into the territory of the Qi state, unstoppable all the way, and killed all the way into the capital of the Qi state, Linzi. King Min of Qi ran to Jucheng and was killed by Nao Chi, a general sent by the Chu state to save the Qi state. Yue Yi was in the Qi state for five years and obtained more than seventy cities of the Qi state, recovering all the lost land of the Yan state, except for the two cities of Ju and Jimo.

It is said that at that time there was a virtuous person in the Qi state named Wang Xie, who was very capable. Governing a country was not a difficult thing for him. Unfortunately, King Min of Qi could not use him, and he only ended up being a farmer in Jin Yi. Although King Min of Qi could not reuse Wang Xie, Wang Xie's reputation was very great, and many people in the country and abroad knew him.

When Yue Yi led the troops and horses into the territory of the Qi state, he ordered, "The virtuous person of the Qi state, Wang Xie, is said to be living in Jin Yi now. Within thirty miles around Jin Yi, our army is not allowed to disturb him. Those who disobey the order will be beheaded!"

Because of Wang Xie, Jin Yi was spared the disturbance of the Yan soldiers.

After a while, Yue Yi had already broken through many cities in the Qi state and obtained a lot of land. The capital of the Qi state had also been broken, and King Min of Qi had also been driven away. The Qi state was not far from being destroyed.

Yue Yi wanted to win over the hearts of the people of the Qi state, so that the cities he had obtained could be kept permanently. There was no better way to win over the hearts of the people than to use the local virtuous people. Therefore, Yue Yi thought of Wang Xie. He thought, "Needless to say, Wang Xie is a virtuous person. Because of him, I did not call the soldiers to go to Jin Yi, which can be considered to be worthy of him. I will now call someone to invite him out, and he will definitely agree."

Yue Yi's messenger arrived in Jin Yi, found Wang Xie's house, and found Wang Xie. He said to Wang Xie, "The junior general has received General Yue's order to invite you, sir. General Yue said, 'You, sir, are the first capable person in the Qi state. I especially invite you, sir, to be a consultant. After the Qi state is pacified, I will report to His Royal Highness the King of Yan and definitely seal you, sir, as a Marquis of Ten Thousand Households.'"

Wang Xie listened, and without any hesitation, immediately replied, "I am a person of the Qi state, and now the Qi state is about to be destroyed, and I am a person of a destroyed country. What use is there for a person of a destroyed country? I only wish to cultivate the land in the Qi state and do not wish to be an official of the Yan state."

Yue Yi's messenger tried to persuade him for a long time, saying so much that his tongue was dry and his lips were parched, but Wang Xie just did not agree. The messenger had no choice but to return to the camp.

Yue Yi's messenger returned to the camp and told Yue Yi what Wang Xie had said. Yue Yi listened and was very unhappy. He pondered for a while and thought of another idea. He then called the messenger again to invite Wang Xie. When he left, Yue Yi said a few words in the messenger's ear.

Yue Yi's messenger arrived in Jin Yi again, arrived at Wang Xie's house, and found Wang Xie again. He said to Wang Xie with a stern face, "The junior general has again received General Yue's order to invite you, sir. General Yue said, 'If you, sir, insist on not going out, I will lead the troops and horses to kill everyone in Jin Yi.' Sir, listen to the junior general's advice and it is better to go out. You will be an official again and protect the lives of the people in this place."

Yue Yi's intention was to intimidate Wang Xie. If Wang Xie was afraid, wouldn't he come out? Who knew that Wang Xie was not afraid of being intimidated.

When Wang Xie heard this, he looked up to the sky and sneered a few times, saying, "A person who loves his own country will never surrender to the enemy in order to become an official or because he is afraid of death. I am a person of the Qi state, and I love the Qi state. I will never leave the Qi state, and I wish the Qi state to be strong. It is a pity that His Royal Highness the King of Qi does not use me. If His Royal Highness the King of Qi used me, you would not come here. His Royal Highness the King of Qi does not use me, and I can only cultivate the land here, but I still do not leave the Qi state. Since the country is about to be destroyed, it is hateful that my strength is too small and the people's hearts are not aligned, and I cannot save the country. Rather than live as a slave of a destroyed country, it is better for you to boil me. There is no need to mention being an official of your Yan state. Fortunately, Yue Yi just wants to see me, this person. Taking my head to let him see is still the same. It also lets him know that the Qi state is not all traitors, but there are still people who cannot be tempted by wealth and honor and cannot be oppressed by force."

After Wang Xie finished speaking, he pushed Yue Yi's messenger out of the door and closed the door. He turned around and went inside, put on his clothes and hat, took a rope, walked to the backyard, looked for a tree, looked at it for a while, and then shouted loudly, "The Emperor of Heaven is above, the ancestors are above, Wang Xie's strength is too small, and he cannot save the country alive. He can only repay the country with death. After death, he must also fulfill his responsibility." After Wang Xie finished speaking, he climbed up the tree, tied his neck to the trunk with the rope, and struggled hard to break his neck.

Wang Xie's death stirred up many people, who all said, "Wang Xie is just an ordinary commoner, and he can do his best to be loyal to the country. What about us, big or small, who are still officials? We do not go to save the country, and we are truly ashamed to death!" Therefore, everyone ran to Jucheng, found King Min of Qi's crown prince, Fa Zhang, and established him as king, uniting with Tian Dan, who was defending Jimo, to fight against the Yan soldiers. Afterwards, Tian Dan used a counter-espionage plan to transfer Yue Yi away and used a fire ox plan to defeat the Yan soldiers, recovering all the lost cities and land, and the Qi state was still so big. All of this was stirred up by Wang Xie's loyalty and righteousness. Wang Xie did not die in vain.

Isaac Merritt Singer (1811-1975)

— Zhong Bao

—Sewing Machine Inventor— The Father Failed Due to Pessimism, The Son Succeeded Due to Optimism

Singer was born in New York, USA, in 1811. His father was a millwright. The family was poor and unable to afford much schooling. Singer had only learned a few characters when he was forced to drop out of school. On the day he left school, his father said to him with tears of sorrow: "Son, I know that making progress requires studying. When I was young, everyone said I was a genius, and I aspired to be an inventor. Unfortunately, I didn't have the opportunity to study, and I don't understand any scientific principles, so I can only be a millwright! I finally have a smart and studious son like you. I should have supported you to study and become an adult. But we are so poor now that even eating bread is a problem. How can I let you go to school? Son, your future destiny may be worse than mine!..." He sobbed and couldn't speak.

At this time, Singer was already a teenager. He understood many human relationships and was optimistic and proactive. He believed his future was limitless, and he didn't want to listen to his father's words. If someone else had said it, he would have covered his ears and left long ago. But because it came from his poor father's mouth, he had to listen. Seeing the old man so sad, he had to express his sympathy. He hurried forward, wiping his father's tears and comforting him: "Son is confident in life, and destiny is in his own hands. Son will definitely succeed as an inventor. What Dad wanted to do but couldn't, Son can do for Dad. Don't worry, leave everything to Son."

The father felt a little relieved and looked at his son standing in front of him, saying slowly: "How can this work? You only have so little schooling!"

Singer said: "Reading is certainly improving the school for convenience. But for those who aspire to study, where can't they read? Why must they go to school? Besides, reading can only give us knowledge, not experience. Experience is indispensable for every inventor. Let me go out to make a living, learn how to live, and get more experience to prepare for invention. Burying oneself in books all day, not understanding what society needs, cannot stimulate the emotion of invention, prompting one to decide what to invent."

"Son, you're right!" the father said happily, "When I was young, although I aspired to be an inventor, because I had little experience, I didn't know the needs of society, and I never resolved to invent anything. Maybe it's because I didn't have a firm will, so I spent my life as a slave to life, achieving nothing? Son, you can take me as a warning. In the future, when you go out to work, learn everything happily and seek more experience. Don't be like me, frowning all day and treating everything as hard labor. As a result, working all year round, not only did I not gain experience, but I also ruined myself. Now I'm prematurely aging, and I can't do anything!" The father said here, with a bitter face, almost crying. Singer quickly diverted the topic, diverting his father's attention, letting him forget his unrepentant mistakes, so as not to suffer.

In fact, Singer had more difficulties than his father when he was younger. His father was able to study well for a few years and do an apprenticeship for a few years. Singer was forced to drop out of school, and as soon as he put down his books, he had to bear the burden of the family. In order to earn money immediately, he had no opportunity to do an apprenticeship and could only prepare to be a skilled worker, doing some unskilled rough work. Rough work takes a lot of effort and pays little, and few people are willing to do it. But Singer, with the determination to seek experience, was not afraid of hardship and worked hard. After doing it for seven years in one breath, he discovered that he was interested in machines, so he went to be a machine apprentice. After only four months of learning, the family had no income, forcing him to quit his apprenticeship and run around for food and clothing. He worked as a machinist in one state and as a clerk in another state: he spent a full nine years of wandering life.

In the process of wandering, Singer worked and studied machines at the same time. At the age of twenty-eight, he invented a rock-drilling machine, followed by a wood metal-carving Machine. After obtaining the patent rights, he raised money to open a factory to manufacture the machines he invented. Unexpectedly, his factory exploded not long after it opened, and the entire factory collapsed along with it, leaving Singer not only bankrupt but also in debt. His relatives and friends were sad for him, but he himself was optimistic as always. He said: "Failure is the mother of success." If I can not be discouraged by failure, and learn from this big lesson, I will study more carefully. Maybe I can grasp some great principles and invent something more valuable."

Singer had a friend named Di Bo'er, who worked in a machine factory in Boston. Seeing that Singer had nowhere to return, he invited him to work together. One evening with few stars, Di Bo'er took Singer's hand and went for a walk. They talked and laughed, unintentionally walking to a street of female seamstresses. There was an open space beside the street, piled with wood ready to build a house. Singer and Di Bo'er sat in the wood pile and talked. They talked enthusiastically about mechanical engineering, about each other's aspirations for invention. When they were happy, Di Bo'er said: "Singer, you are good, you have already invented two machines. I don't know when I will be able to make some achievements." Singer replied: "What is this worth? I never considered those two machines I created as inventions, because they have too little effect. When I can invent a machine that can benefit people all over the world, especially the poor, I will be satisfied. But I don't know what to invent now. You..."

It was almost midnight, and there were no pedestrians on the street. It was quiet all around, leaving only Singer's clear voice. Unexpectedly, someone suddenly sang nearby, the tune was sad and moving. Singer began to interrupt the topic and listened quietly. He only heard a sad woman's voice singing: Fingers are pierced, dare not say tired; Eyes are swollen and red, dare not be greedy for sleep. Poor seamstresses, hands inseparable from needle and thread, Thousands of stitches of hard sewing, One day, three meals, hard to get enough. Year after year, making wedding clothes for others, Who knows the bitterness in this! Singer was very moved and asked Di Bo'er with tears in his eyes: "Who is singing?"

Di Bo'er said coldly: "Don't you know this street is a street of female seamstresses? Who else would sing besides the female seamstresses?" Singer felt even more uncomfortable when he heard his indifferent tone. He couldn't help thinking: "Female seamstresses are also human beings, why are they so miserable, and no one is helping them; even a sentimental person like Di Bo'er doesn't know to express sympathy to them?..." He lowered his head and thought for a while, and suddenly came up with a reason. He asked Di Bo'er: "Is it okay for me to invent a sewing machine?"

Di Bo'er laughed and said: "I thought you were thinking about something, it turned out you were planning to help the female seamstresses!" At this time, the sky was cloudless and the moon was bright as a picture. Singer saw Di Bo'er's cunning smile very clearly. But he was not afraid of Di Bo'er making fun of him, and still said frankly: "I really have this intention, is it impossible?" Di Bo'er said: "It's not impossible, but it's definitely a difficult thing. In the past few decades, I don't know how many people have wanted to invent a sewing machine, but they all failed. — Maybe it's waiting for you to invent it." Di Bo'er gave another cunning smile. Singer said: "Don't joke, let's discuss the matter of inventing a sewing machine." The singing started again. Di Bo'er was afraid that the sentimental Singer would be sad again after hearing the sad tone, so he forcibly pulled him back to the factory.

Seeing that Singer was so enthusiastic about inventing a sewing machine and that his plan was well-organized, Di Bo'er borrowed forty yuan to give him as capital, and asked the factory owner to borrow a corner of the workshop to give him a place to experiment with inventing a sewing machine.

Singer was grateful for Di Bo'er's help, cherished his confidant, and worked even harder. He worked in the field early and late, sleeping only three or four hours a day and eating one meal. Even this meal was nothing more than two or three slices of bread and a cup of salt water. He held a hammer all day long, hammering machines, until two o'clock in the night before letting go, shrinking into a dormitory like a chicken coop to sleep. He jumped down to work before dawn. After several months of this, he saw that his machine could turn, bite cloth, and sew. He was overjoyed and ran out to tell people.

As soon as this news spread, many people ran out and surrounded Singer's workshop, asking Singer to perform for them. Singer was of course very happy to obey. Unexpectedly, during the performance, the machine suddenly became awkward with him and could not bite the cloth. When it could bite the cloth, it could not sew. At this time, some scolded him for lying and deceiving people, hanging a sheep's head and selling dog meat. Some covered their mouths and snickered, mocking him in every possible way. Singer was so anxious that he was sweating profusely and had no way to defend himself. He was so ashamed and angry that he almost committed suicide. But thinking that his shame could not be washed away by suicide, he lowered his head and continued to work. After working hard for a few more months, he finally invented the sewing machine. At this time, all the people who used to laugh at him and scold him ran over to apologize and congratulate him. His sewing machine quickly became popular all over the world. How could the beneficiaries be limited to the female seamstress who sang sadly on that moonlit night?

Publishing Industry

On the Issue of Textbook Compilation and Monopoly

— Du Xiu

Recently, the author received a relatively reliable rumor that the compilation of textbooks will be handled exclusively by the Ministry of Education, and each bookstore will not be allowed to compile freely. The distribution of textbooks will be entrusted by the Ministry of Education to a certain bookstore for sale. Therefore, each bookstore is now vying for this monopoly issue.

The author does not know whether this news is true; even if it is true, the author does not know what the implementation method is. Because the nature of this event is too important, therefore, I dare to offer my humble opinions for the reference of the highest educational authorities and people from all walks of life.

The power to compile textbooks should be unified urgently. This is the author's consistent claim. However, it is easier to unify the power to compile, but it is difficult to ensure that the content is perfect after unification. Therefore, the problem lies in how to compile. Assuming that the needs of the national conditions, the conditions of the region, and the environment of children are not carefully considered, then the compiled textbooks will definitely not realize our ideals, this is one point; at the same time, the determination of the principles of textbook compilation depends on the careful discussion of experts, and the actual compilation work also requires all kinds of practical experience in teaching. How to take care of both parties when compiling is the second point; With the vast territory and ununified cultural level of our country, it is impossible to adapt to the needs of the whole country with one kind of textbook, so how can we make each region not feel difficulty, this is the third point. These three major issues are three prerequisites for compiling textbooks. Without proper statutory provisions for these three prerequisites, we can never imagine that the unified textbooks will have perfect results, this is regarding the compilation aspect.

After the textbooks are compiled, there is the issue of sales. The author believes that if a certain bookstore is entrusted with the exclusive sales, the disadvantages are endless, and it will definitely cause all kinds of unnecessary misunderstandings. The best way is that the Ministry of Education has a provision for any kind of textbook, all paper, typesetting, cover, font, etc., and the price is also set by the Ministry of Education. Any bookstore can publish and sell after being approved by the Ministry of Education, and a certain amount of royalties will be drawn according to the number of sales. The royalties drawn will be used as remuneration for the compilers of textbooks. This method can eliminate the hoarding after the exclusive sales of each bookstore; second, it can eliminate the competition of each bookstore; third, it can eliminate all kinds of unnecessary misunderstandings; third, it can reduce a little burden for general students and parents.

The unified compilation of textbooks and the sales issue after the unified compilation are indeed important matters and should be urgently realized. However, the implementation methods really need to be considered with great care.

The Problems of Tomorrow's Kangzang, Yunnan and Guangxi (Continued)

— Wu Qiyun

By Fang Qiuwei, Published by World Publishing

Such a large Northeast is now taken by Japan; such a large Northwest, if Japan's westward policy is rapidly advanced, then it can also be serious immediately; if the Southwest is not set up with plans, this large Kangzang, Yunnan and Guangxi is also in the bag of the great powers. China's border problems did not occur today, but the state of serious danger is no greater than today!

At the same time, a country has a whole chain. The problem in the Northeast is not the issue of the survival of the Northeast, but the issue of the survival of the entire China; the Northwest is also the same, and the Southwest must be the same? Moreover, the international ties of the Northeast problem are still few. Once the Southwest problem occurs, it will inevitably involve the Northwest problem, forming a major conflict with the great powers related to the Far East. The result of the conflict is often to go to the road of partition through war or spoils, affecting the survival of the entire China!

To hope to solve the Southwest problem, we should start from understanding the Southwest and studying the Southwest. Then, the author respectfully recommends this book "The Problems of Tomorrow's Kangzang, Yunnan and Guangxi" to the general public.

The book starts from the inevitability of imperialists invading small and weak nations, and then analyzes the current situation of Tibet, Xikang, Yunnan, and Guangxi from a geographical point of view; then it talks about the history of British and French intrusions in the Southwest, as well as the current situation of invasion; finally, it adds a comprehensive comparison and analysis. After reading this book, not only can you get a general concept, but you can also get involved in specialized research. The book has 100,000 words and is priced at 50 cents, published by World Publishing. (End)

The publication has no background and is purely for the purpose of promoting the aviation industry and advocating aviation to save the country.
